British Style Small Ball to be Demonstration Game: Now Being Compiled

In order to promote small ball sports, the Chinese National Small Ball Association, which is actively preparing for its establishment, will launch a league using British-style small balls. It is found that this game is still new in China, and its interest and simplicity are better than our country's current small rubber. It is learned that the association, in view of the necessity of publicity and demonstration, has hired experts to compile a special book based on the British-style small ball regulations. Once published, in addition to widely distributing it to all sectors, a demonstration game will be held at Shen Garden on Yanping Road to promote it. An excerpt of the rules is as follows: (1) Player qualifications: Based on age, height, and weight, the following three groups are specified. "Adult Group" players must be 62 inches tall, weigh 115 pounds, and be 19 years of age or older to qualify. "Youth Group" players must be 66 inches or less, 60 inches or more, weigh 115 pounds or less, 90 pounds or more, and be 15 years of age or older and 19 years of age or younger to qualify. "Children Group" players must be 62 inches or less, 58 inches or more, weigh 90 pounds or less, 75 pounds or more, and be 12 years of age or older and 15 years of age or younger to qualify. (2) Player distribution: Each side is limited to 7 or 9 players (depending on the size of the court). If there are less than 6 players, the game cannot be played. The positions are: two center forwards (also known as left and right forwards), one left and right winger each, two center backs (or left and right midfielders), one left and right defender each, and one goalkeeper. Players who are injured and leave the field can be replaced by substitutes, but only two are allowed. (3) Court layout: The court is a rectangular plane, suitable for grass or hard ground. The maximum dimensions are 100 yards long, the goalposts are 6 to 7 yards wide, the height is 7 feet, and the width of the crossbar and two posts shall not exceed 5 inches. (4) Ball and shoes: The ball is round (about half the size of a small football), with a rubber bladder placed in a yellow leather shell, filled with air to make it expand. The weight of a light ball is at least 6 ounces, and the weight of a heavy ball is at most 8 ounces. The circumference of the ball is 20 to 22 inches. The shoes are required to be cloth shoes or rubber shoes. Players wearing football shoes are not allowed to participate. (5) Game time: "Adult Group" is 70 minutes, "Youth Group" is 60 minutes, and "Children Group" is 50 minutes, with a 10-minute break in the middle. If the referee gives special permission, the extension or reduction is not subject to this rule. (6) All other aspects are suitable for football rules to conduct the game.

Education News

Statistics of School-Age Children in Chahar Province: Totaling 142,820, with 66,697 Enrolled

Zhangjiakou Quick Dispatch: Chahar Province has a narrow area, with only sixteen counties and three administrative bureaus in the entire province. Since last year when bandit troops invaded northern Chahar, six counties including Zhangbei and Dolun, and the three administrative bureaus of Shangyi, Huade, and Chongli, have formed a special region. They have not yet returned to normal, coupled with the barren land and poor people, and insufficient financial resources, resulting in the lack of significant results in administrative areas such as construction and education. Regarding education, although the Chahar provincial authorities are in this situation, they are still proceeding step by step according to the established plan, especially actively promoting compulsory education, sparing no effort. As for the province's school-age children, as well as those who have enrolled and those who have not, there are currently no detailed statistics because the 25th year of the Republic has not yet begun. The report from the 24th year of the Republic recently submitted by the Education Department is considered accurate. According to the survey of children in the province in the 23rd year of the Republic, there were 47,966 school-age children in the nine counties and bureaus of northern Chahar, with 8,726 enrolled and 39,240 not enrolled. Adding the ten counties in southern Chahar, the provincial total was 190,786, with 75,423 enrolled, 104,437 not enrolled, and 10,926 postponed or exempted from school. According to the statistics of the 24th year of the Republic, excluding the counties and bureaus of northern Chahar, there are a total of 142,820 school-age children (ages 6 to 12), with 66,697 enrolled, 65,197 not enrolled, 7,986 postponed, and 1,940 exempted. The exact numbers of children's ages in the ten counties of southern Chahar are listed below:

Wanquan: Ages 6 to 8, 2,653 enrolled, 3,086 not enrolled, 358 postponed, 140 exempted, totaling 6,237. Ages 9 to 12, 5,113 enrolled, 3,461 not enrolled, 596 postponed, 272 exempted, totaling 9,443. The total number of school-age children in the county is 15,679.

Xuanhua: Ages 6 to 8, 3,553 enrolled, 4,287 not enrolled, 1,022 postponed, 196 exempted, totaling 9,026. Ages 9 to 12, 5,956 enrolled, 4,585 not enrolled, 1,166 postponed, 429 exempted, totaling 12,136. The total number of school-age children in the county is 21,162.

Yuxian: Ages 6 to 8, 4,841 enrolled, 8,726 not enrolled, 748 postponed, 90 exempted, totaling 14,405. Ages 9 to 12, 9,201 enrolled, 7,693 not enrolled, 720 postponed, 193 exempted, totaling 17,818. The total number of school-age children in the county is 32,223.

Huailai: Ages 6 to 8, 3,583 enrolled, 1,940 not enrolled, 848 postponed, 358 exempted, totaling 6,729. Ages 9 to 12, 6,148 enrolled, 1,715 not enrolled, 741 postponed, 561 exempted, totaling 9,165. The total number of school-age children in the county is 15,894.

Zhuolu: Ages 6 to 8, 1,790 enrolled, 2,621 not enrolled, 68 postponed, 30 exempted, totaling 4,509. Ages 9 to 12, 3,759 enrolled, 2,044 not enrolled, 106 postponed, 90 exempted, totaling 5,999. The total number of school-age children in the county is 10,508.

Huaian: Ages 6 to 8, 1,664 enrolled, 3,845 not enrolled, 379 postponed, 33 exempted, totaling 5,921. Ages 9 to 12, 5,101 enrolled, 3,989 not enrolled, 17 postponed, 84 exempted, totaling 9,152. The total number of school-age children in the county is 15,073.

Yangyuan: Ages 6 to 8, 865 enrolled, 3,441 not enrolled, 44 postponed, 10 exempted, totaling 4,361. Ages 9 to 12, 2,275 enrolled, 4,240 not enrolled, 70 postponed, 23 exempted, totaling 6,608. The total number of school-age children in the county is 10,969.

Yanqing: Ages 6 to 8, 815 enrolled, 1,480 not enrolled, 153 postponed, 10 exempted, totaling 2,458. Ages 9 to 12, 2,675 enrolled, 1,523 not enrolled, 148 postponed, 17 exempted, totaling 4,363. The total number of school-age children in the county is 6,821.

Draft Organizational Regulations for National Nanchang Zhongzheng Medical College

(Nanjing 1st Dispatch) The Ministry of Education is planning to establish the National Nanchang Zhongzheng Medical College. Due to its large scale, it has decided to establish a design committee to be responsible for planning everything. Draft organizational regulations have been prepared, stipulating that the committee will have nine to eleven members, including one representative from the Ministry of Education, one representative from the Health Administration, two representatives from the Medical Education Committee, one preparatory director, one director of the Jiangxi Provincial Health Experiment Bureau, and three to five experts hired by the Ministry of Education to form the committee jointly. Letters have been sent to relevant agencies to select representatives, and the committee will be established within the month.

Wusong Merchant Marine College Commemorates the 7th Anniversary of its Revival

The Wusong Merchant Marine College, directly under the Ministry of Communications, was founded in the late Qing Dynasty. It was suspended for a period of time and revived in the 18th year of the Republic, and it has been seven years since then. Graduates from previous years have all been assigned to senior crew positions and have been praised by the maritime industry. The current principal, Mr. Liu Yonggao, is a famous naval veteran. Since taking office, he has been following the instructions of Minister Yu of the Ministry of Communications and has been working hard to reorganize the school affairs. More than 30 graduates from the navigation and machinery departments this year were introduced by Principal Liu to various maritime administrative agencies and shipping companies after graduating this summer, and they have all been employed. It can also be seen that the school's cultivation of maritime talents has been highly trusted by various sectors of maritime administration and shipping. The anniversary of the school's revival was celebrated on the same day. Because it was a time of national crisis, no extravagant activities were held. At 10:00 am, Principal Liu led all staff and students to hold a memorial ceremony in the auditorium. Director Wu of the Shanghai Maritime Affairs Bureau, representing the Ministry of Communications, attended the school. After the ceremony was held as scheduled, Principal Liu reported on the school's founding and revival. Then, Director Wu spoke on behalf of the Ministry of Communications, detailing the relationship between the school and maritime rights and shipping, and encouraging students to study hard. The Ministry has great hopes for them. Subsequently, guests including President Weng of Tongji University and Mr. Tao Yishan, representative of the Shanghai Military Training Association, gave speeches one after another, with many enlightening words. In the afternoon, sports meetings were held in the rain. The various programs were also quite special and wonderful. The meeting ended in the fading twilight.

Special Article: Shanghai YWCA (Manuscript from the YWCA)

People's Education

Eliminating one illiterate is increasing the strength of national self-renewal by one point, and it is also strengthening the blow against the enemy's aggression. Ladies and gentlemen of Shanghai! Do you like to increase the strength of national self-renewal? Are you also willing to strengthen the blow against the enemy's aggression? As long as you save a few 2.65 yuan in legal tender in a year according to your strength, you can eliminate one - two - three - hundreds of illiterates. Why? According to the experience of our Shanghai YWCA in establishing women's people's schools over the years (since 1923, we have opened dozens of civil education classes in various districts of Shanghai), as long as there is a classroom (at least one, preferably two or three), and one or two enthusiastic teachers with national ideas, and prepare some funds each semester (100 yuan or several hundred yuan), you can enroll dozens or hundreds of illiterate women students, open classes to teach them (it was very difficult to enroll students before, but after having results, we only dislike the small rooms and too many people, and now it is becoming more and more crowded). After four or five months or a year of serious teaching and training (only two hours of classes per day), students will be able to write, calculate, read simple newspapers, make simple speeches, practice clean hygiene, and also change their old-fashioned ideas, knowing that women are also people - important people, knowing their own family environment, social conditions, national status, foreign enemy aggression, and also changing their lives, knowing the importance of group life, the relationship of mutual assistance and mutual force, and all the common sense that a person should have, it can be said that everything is there. According to our statistics, the cost of cultivating such a very simple and very ordinary citizen is at most 2.65 yuan in legal tender. Compared with the schooling fees of aristocratic education, young masters and young ladies, at least several hundred yuan or nearly a thousand yuan per semester, there is a real difference between heaven and earth. Isn't this a very easy thing to do? It is a pity that too few people pay attention to it.

Ladies and gentlemen of Shanghai, please rise up and jointly undertake the basic work of saving the country. We hope that the illiterates in Shanghai will be enlightened by your grace and walk into the path of light. Your merits are truly immeasurable.

Our women's people's school this semester has four districts, divided into morning and evening classes. There are 444 students in the spring and 788 students in the autumn, totaling 1,232 people. Our strength is only these. Please help us!

Adult Education

As the saying goes, "Live and learn," and "While there is still breath, there is no room for relaxation." This is to instruct people that the world's knowledge is infinite, and do not be ashamed to stop learning because you are an adult. Therefore, the adult education department of the Shanghai YWCA specializes in implementing various educational undertakings for adult members and adult non-members, so that older women can still keep up with the trend and have the opportunity to contact society, so as to avoid the danger of natural elimination, and with the unity of this organization, they can develop their talents and implement their long-cherished aspirations to love the country. The general outline of adult education is briefly described below.

(1) Remedial Classes: We know that adult women must have family responsibilities, or other reasons, and cannot be outside all day for classes, so we specially open various remedial classes, such as Chinese, English, French, German, Japanese, Chinese and foreign cooking, handicraft, sewing, first aid, nanny class, typing and shorthand, piano, violin, social dance, tap dance, etc. Each subject is one hour a day, or two or three hours a week, so that they will not neglect family affairs because of learning, and will not forget their studies because of family affairs, and the opportunity to study can increase new knowledge, meet new friends, to get rid of the monotony of life, and the pain of boredom.

(2) Gymnasium: Women in Shanghai, where land is at a premium, rarely have fitness exercises other than laboring in household affairs and working in public affairs. In view of the importance of women's sports, the Association has specially opened a large gymnasium behind the Association on Jing'an Temple Road, which is divided into tennis, volleyball, basketball, etc., and also has swimming (borrowing the swimming pool of the Navy Youth Association) as a place for women from all walks of life to exercise their bodies in their spare time and after household affairs.

(3) Research Discussion and Lecture Meeting: Organize groups to study current affairs, discuss family affairs, lecture on international trends, religious truths, and other important groups, as the basis for improving and assisting the family, society, and country.

(4) Visits, Travel, and Social Music Concerts: We want to develop their interest in outdoor life, cultivate their proper entertainment habits, point out the way to common sense, and connect their mutual assistance and unity, so there are visits to famous factories, travel to scenic spots, and the initiation of social music concerts.

(5) Reading Room: The Association prepares a small number of books and various newspapers and magazines for the browsing of the Association's members.

Local News

Provincial Bank Group Organized; Implementation to Begin on New Year's Day; First to Interconnect Remittances and Exchange Auxiliary Currency Notes; Economic Interconnection First, Then Agricultural and Commercial Development

According to Xin Sheng News Agency, the local banks or provincial banks in Zhejiang, Jiangsu, Jiangxi, Anhui, and other provinces, after being stipulated by the Ministry of Finance to be able to issue auxiliary currency notes, the rules for printing auxiliary currency notes have been promulgated by the Ministry. Now, the Jiangsu Farmers Bank and the Jiangsu Bank have jointly issued 3 million yuan to circulate in the market. The 500,000 yuan of auxiliary currency notes previously issued by the Zhejiang Local Bank has been taken over by the Issuance Preparation Management Committee, and 3 million yuan newly approved by the Ministry will be issued on New Year's Day. The Anhui Local Bank has been approved by the Ministry to issue 2.5 million yuan of auxiliary currency notes, which will be issued on New Year's Day. The Jiangxi Yumin Bank has submitted the auxiliary currency notes that have been issued to the Ministry of Finance for filing.

Group Organization

The business of provincial banks or local banks is mainly to act as agents for provincial and county treasuries, develop agriculture and commerce in the province, and connect remittances between counties. Now, Xu Enpei, general manager of Zhejiang Local Bank, Qian Chengxin, deputy manager of Jiangxi Yumin Bank, and Cheng Zhenji, head of Anhui Local Bank, etc., have planned a group organization. After exchanging opinions, they have begun to proceed. The first step is for provincial banks or local banks to interconnect remittances. The second step is for provincial banks or local banks to exchange auxiliary currency notes, so that the economies of the provinces are interconnected, and then seek the development of agriculture, industry, and commerce in the provinces.

Implementation on New Year's Day

Now, Zhejiang Local Bank and Jiangxi Yumin Bank have first drafted a contract for mutual remittance and exchange of auxiliary currency notes between the two provinces. After the banks of the two provinces submit it to the business meeting of the head office for approval, they will sign it and implement it on New Year's Day. As for Cheng Zhenji, head of Anhui Local Bank, and Xu Enpei, general manager of Zhejiang Local Bank, they have negotiated the interconnection of remittances between the two provinces and are drafting a contract. However, the date of implementation has not yet been determined.

Zhonghui and Jiangzhe Two Banks to Merge and Operate Today

In order to increase strength and expand business, the Zhonghui and Jiangzhe Banks of this city held a shareholders' meeting on October 26 to establish a merger, and elected Du Yuesheng, Qian Xinzhi, Chen Guangfu, Jiang Yiping, etc. as directors and supervisors. Everything has been prepared and the merger will be implemented today. It will be renamed Zhonghui Bank Co., Ltd., and the Zhonghui Bank on Avenue Edward VII will be changed to the head office, and the original site of Jiangzhe Bank on Jiangxi Road will be changed to the Zhonghui Bank branch, and business will begin. The total amount of bank capital will be merged to 3.5 million yuan. The scope of business still includes deposits, savings, securities, real estate, guarantees, etc., and special attention will be paid to the savings business. A special savings department will be established, and funds will be allocated separately, and the accounting will be independent, so as to expand the business. Du Yuesheng will be the chairman and general manager, and Wu Qiding, Zhou Wenrui, Qian Xinzhi, and Zhang Fayao will be standing directors.

Local Association Cables to Request Relaxation of Rice and Grain Ban in Jiangsu and Zhejiang

The Shanghai Local Association believes that the express ban on the export of rice and grain from Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces has greatly affected the social economy. On October 31, it telegraphed the chairmen of the two provinces, requesting the ban to be relaxed. The text reads: "To Chairman Chen and Chairman Huang of the Provincial Government of Zhenjiang and Hangzhou, this year, Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and other provinces have all celebrated a bumper harvest, and transportation is convenient, which can promote the circulation of rice and grain and enrich rural finance. Now, it is heard that the provincial government is carefully accumulating grain and expressly prohibits it from being exported from the province, which may lead to overproduction and a sharp drop in rice prices. Areas that need rice may worry about not being able to supply it. Shanghai needs rice and grain from other provinces. Hearing this ban, merchants have become panicked. It is believed that exports to foreign countries must be prohibited, but domestic circulation should still be allowed. The members of our association all have this idea. Therefore, we specifically telegraphed to request you to consider the relationship between farmers and merchants and the social economy, and withdraw the express ban on the export of rice and grain from the province. On the other hand, strictly prohibit exports to foreign countries. Respectfully await your decision and reply." Shanghai Local Association, Du Yong, Qian Yongming, Wang Xiaolai, et al.

Gu Xin-yi Returned to Shanghai Yesterday from Nanjing; the Rice Seizure in Zhejiang Province Has Been Ordered Stopped by the Executive Yuan; the Ministry of Industries Expressed Acceptance of Shanghai Merchants' Requests

Gu Xin-yi, Chairman of the Shanghai Grain Merchants' Association, regarding the matter of the Jiangsu and Zhejiang provincial governments prohibiting rice exports from their provinces, went to Nanjing on the 30th, along with a petition from the association, to request that the Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Industries order the Jiangsu and Zhejiang authorities to rescind the ban. Mr. Gu having completed his business in Nanjing, left the city yesterday morning and arrived in Shanghai at 2 p.m. A reporter from the Central News Agency paid him a special visit to inquire about the situation regarding his petition to the Yuan and Ministry in Nanjing. According to Mr. Gu, in addition to representing the grain industry in participating in the airplane donation ceremony, he also petitioned the Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Industries regarding the Jiangsu and Zhejiang authorities' prohibition of rice exports. He arrived in Nanjing the day before yesterday (the 31st), and after participating in the airplane donation ceremony, first went to the Executive Yuan to petition. Secretary-General Weng Wenhao received him, and in addition to personally presenting the association's petition, he also described the situation of the people's food supply in Shanghai, and how the prohibition of rice exports by the Jiangsu and Zhejiang authorities would likely cause panic in Shanghai's food supply. The Secretary-General agreed that prohibiting rice exports was indeed contrary to the central government's original intention of relieving rural areas and regulating food supplies. However, the Jiangsu and Zhejiang authorities had not yet reported the matter of prohibiting rice exports to Nanjing, but since the association had submitted a report stating that rice seizures had occurred in Zhejiang, the Executive Yuan would first issue an order to stop them. As for the association's proposed method of exporting rice, there were still some inappropriate aspects, and a central government review should be conducted before any regulations were made. He then went to the Ministry of Industries, where Director Xu Tinghu of the Agricultural Affairs Department and Director Zhang Yi'ou of the Commercial Affairs Department received him and expressed acceptance of the requests of the Shanghai merchants. Furthermore, the Ministry of Finance happened to be convening a meeting of relevant ministries and commissions at 3 p.m. that afternoon to discuss the unified control of food, so the two directors took the petition of the Shanghai merchants to the meeting for reference. It is understood that the result of the discussion was that everyone agreed that prohibiting exports was inappropriate, but that in the future there should be accurate statistics on transportation and sales, so that the unified control of food could be gradually implemented in the future. As for the detailed measures, they still needed to be carefully planned.

All Catholic Churches in the City Prayed for Premier Chiang Yesterday

For Premier Chiang's 50th birthday celebration, the Catholic Church, in addition to Archbishop Cai representing all Catholics sending a telegram of congratulations and promoting the donation of ambulances, Bishop Haou of Shanghai notified all priests and Catholics under his jurisdiction a decade ago to offer public prayers for China and its leader on the Sunday before and after Chiang's birthday. Subsequently, because last Sunday coincided with the national funeral period for the late Chairman Hu, and the whole country was in mourning, it was not appropriate to hold extravagant celebrations, so everything was uniformly changed to November 1st for a fervent celebration. Yesterday morning, more than 20 Catholic churches in the city rang their bells loudly and in unison, as if it were a great holiday. Although it was raining, Catholics flocked to the nearest Catholic churches to participate in the Mass and prayers with great enthusiasm. The churches were decorated with red velvet banners, fresh flowers, and candles, and the displays were extremely luxurious. From 5 a.m. to noon, priests took turns holding Mass, preaching the principles of loving and saving the country and supporting the government, and encouraging believers to pray for the country's difficulties and the leader, asking God to bless Premier Chiang with health, longevity, and peace, and to grant China national prosperity, peace, and abundant harvests. The Catholic churches in Xinbeimen, Rue Lupan, Xujiahui, Dongjiadu, and Nanxun Road all had musical performances, and the streets were crowded with people and carriages, making for a grand scene.

The Shanghai Suburban Rural Improvement Area Reviewed Achievements Yesterday, Held an Achievement Exhibition, and Reviewed Mass Activities

The Shanghai Suburban Rural Improvement Area, in order to review the past and encourage the future, specially convened an achievement exhibition yesterday (the 1st) at 9 a.m. at Zhaojiatang, north of Zhuanqiao on the Shanghai-Minhang Road, braving the rain, and held a grand ceremony, with an unprecedented grand occasion. The following is a compilation of the various situations:

A Glimpse of the Venue

The venue was located at Zhaojiatang, north of Zhuanqiao on the Shanghai-Minhang Road. A temporary reception station was set up for guests to get on and off. A white cloth banner was placed at the entrance, with the words "Shanghai Suburban Rural Improvement Area Visit Inside" written on it. Four police officers specially dispatched by the Shanghai County Public Security Bureau stood proudly on both sides. Upon entering, one immediately caught sight of the plaza. A simple stage was set up in the center of the field, and several exhibition rooms for air defense and anti-poisoning were specially activated in the Zhaojiatang Office of the Shanghai Suburban Rural Improvement Area (inside Hongying No. 2 Elementary School).

Participating Guests

Guests continued to arrive from 9 a.m. yesterday. The groups included Zhang Yi, Supervisory Committee Member of the Shanghai County Party Headquarters; Chen Jiapu, Executive Committee Member; Wang Gongyu, Inspector of the Songjiang District; Jiang Wenyu, Huang Renzhi, and Yang Weiyu of the China Vocational Education Society; Ye Hongying, Principal of Hongying Elementary School; Lou Jiaji, Tang Maohuai, and Xu Shuzheng of the Shanghai West People's Education Experimental Area; Li Zhifu of the Shanghai County Government; Zhang Xinfu of the Shanhai Institute of Technology; and more than 400 guests including Shen Airong, Shen Jiucheng, Lin Meiyan, Shi Ansheng, Shi Yangyong, and Yao Huiquan.

Chairman's Report

Starting at 1:30 p.m., the opening meeting was held in the plaza. Zhang Fengshan was publicly elected as chairman. After performing the rituals, Chairman Zhang first gave a report, saying in brief, "Respected officials, respected guests, respected comrades, today the Shanghai Suburban Rural Improvement Area is holding a village activity, and especially the national defense exhibition is even more meaningful. I am very honored and very grateful that you have taken the time to participate in the rain. China is a country based on agriculture. Of course, everything in the countryside has a major relationship with the country. Just think, China's land is so large, why is it not enough? And why are the people so weak? If we want to make the country productive and revitalized, we must first implement the Baojia system. But it needs the promotion of education. The Shanghai Suburban Rural Improvement Area is to ensure that every adult, child, and woman has the right to receive compulsory education. Although there have been no achievements in the two years since this area was implemented, the reduction of illiteracy is still fulfilling our responsibility. We hope that the officials and guests who are present will provide practical guidance to jointly promote the construction of a new countryside."

General Secretary's Report

Only About 40 Silk Factories in Shanghai are Operating; Due to a Shortage of Raw Materials

Scarce Wheat Sources; Flour Mills Lack Raw Materials

The Xin Xin News Agency reports that flour mills in Shanghai have recently experienced a scarcity of wheat sources, resulting in a significant shortage of raw materials. They want to purchase foreign wheat, but the prices are too high, so they have no choice but to reduce production. However, demand from various regions is very strong, causing market prices to rise daily. The reporter has investigated and recorded the situation as follows:

Sharp Decline in Sources

The raw materials for flour mills in Shanghai, in addition to foreign wheat, mostly depend on wheat produced in Gaoyou, Taizhou, and Yancheng counties in northern Jiangsu. The annual amount transported to Shanghai is estimated at about 1.7 to 1.8 million bags. This year, the amount transported to Shanghai has reached only 50% to 60% of that amount. Recently, the sales of flour to Guangdong, Tianjin, and Southeast Asia have been brisk, and demand is very strong, resulting in the wheat arriving in Shanghai being insufficient for the consumption of various mills. Moreover, the wheat stored in various places in northern Jiangsu is affected by shallow water, difficult transportation, and the fact that farmers must wait for good prices, so the sources have suddenly become scarce, with only 70,000 to 80,000 bags arriving daily.

Factories Reduce Production

Various flour mills, due to the limited wheat sources and the significant shortage of raw materials, and the fact that various grain firms also have no inventory to hoard, making sourcing very difficult, although flour sales are brisk and market prices are high, they are ultimately unable to produce at full capacity to meet the market due to the scarcity of raw materials, so they have no choice but to reluctantly reduce production. Factories such as Fuxin, Fufeng, and Yuxing are all in a state of reduced production or intermittent operation.

Did Not Purchase Foreign Wheat

Each year, the raw materials needed by various flour mills, in addition to domestic wheat, include foreign wheat, which accounts for 40% to 50%. According to sources in the grain industry, this year, due to the poor harvests of American wheat, the quoted prices are very high. Although there are rumors that Australian wheat may be exported, there is no definite news yet. Therefore, various flour mills have not yet placed orders with foreign merchants because the selling price of foreign wheat is too different from that of domestic wheat, making it too uneconomical.

Bank of China and Bank of Communications Prepare to Handle National Rice Transportation and Discounting; Detailed Measures Have Been Drafted by the Two Banks; Negotiations Will Be Held Within Days, Starting with Hunan Rice

The Xin Xin News Agency reports that the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications, in order to assist the government in regulating the people's food supply, have jointly established a consortium with the Bank of Shanghai, Continental Bank, Jin Cheng Bank, Zhongnan Bank, Salt Industry Bank, National Products Bank, Guohua Bank, and the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau to handle national rice transportation and discounting loans. After a consultation, it was decided to underwrite the three major principles of discounting. The total loan amount is tentatively set at 10 million yuan. In order to save expenses, it is not intended to establish a formal banking syndicate, and the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications are publicly elected as representatives to be responsible for handling the matter. All detailed measures have been drafted by the two banks, and after a second consultation, they will be implemented. It is understood that the loan measures have long been drafted. However, Director Yang of the Second Division of the Bank of China, who is in charge of the matter, returned to his hometown for personal reasons, so a second meeting could not be convened. Mr. Yang has now returned to Shanghai, and it is planned to invite the participating banks to a meeting within days to make a decision. It is heard that the loan procedures are quite simple. All domestic rice and grain that has been inspected and approved by the Ministry of Industry, and rice merchants who have a good reputation, can apply to the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications' branches in various places. If, after review, the regulations are met, the applicant will submit the bill of lading, insurance policy, invoice, etc., and the syndicate will first provide 80% of the discounting price. After the rice is transported to the destination, the purchaser will repay the loan. The syndicate will only collect 7% interest as a commission. However, it has been decided that the first step will be to handle the discounting of Hunan rice transported to Guangdong, and then gradually expand it in the future.

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Requests Insurance Companies to Fairly Assess and Compensate

Bao Feng Ginseng Shop, a member of the Shanghai Marine Products & Edible Bird's Nest Guild, suffered a significant loss in June of this year when the Yong Yu Tai Ginseng Shop next door was careless and caught fire. Although Bao Feng Ginseng Shop was not affected by the fire itself, water was poured into and accumulated in its storage rooms during the firefighting. The insurance company did not assess and compensate for the loss, so the guild sent a letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to negotiate with the insurance companies. The text of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce's letter to Gong Yu & Sun Insurance Company, etc., is as follows:

Respected Sirs,

According to the Shanghai Marine Products & Edible Bird's Nest Guild's letter of the 28th of this month, its member Bao Feng Ginseng Shop stated in its letter that at 6:10 p.m. on June 7th of this year, the Yong Yu Tai Ginseng Shop next door was careless and caught fire. Thanks to the fire department's quick rescue, the fire did not spread. Bao Feng Ginseng Shop's fire insurance of 200,000 yuan, was not enough to cover the water damage to its goods, which was valued at more than 20,000 yuan. The San Yi Public Notary Office sent personnel to investigate, but its assessment seemed to show favoritism, arguing that there was less water accumulation on the third floor and more on the second floor. The fire department's priority was to suppress the fire, so the water pressure focused on one side. Bao Feng Ginseng Shop's roof is a concrete platform, with a gas shed next to it. Due to this sudden attack, the water entered from the gas shed and leaked along the west side of the gas shed. The wooden floors of the three floors below were not heavily damaged, because the damage came from water seeping down. The two cement rooms on the second floor accumulated about two or three inches of water, because one side of the gas cylinder in that layer was not separated by wooden boards, and only had wooden fences for cover, making it very easy for water to enter Bao Feng Ginseng Shop's storage room, which was located there. As for the lower room, there were also three or four inches of water accumulation, which came from the gas cylinder. The power of the water that poured in can be imagined. So far, several months have passed without a resolution. It is unclear what facts the San Yi Public Notary Office based its opinion on, and the office stubbornly insisted on its bias. Bao Feng Ginseng Shop provided documents and evidence to the best of its ability, but the office arbitrarily refused to acknowledge the proper reasons why the insurance company was not compensating for the losses, causing great loss to the business. This is not only contrary to legal principles, but also contrary to human sentiment. Bao Feng Ginseng Shop took out fire insurance policies with six companies - Kung Yih, Sun, North Manchu, Anglo-American, Paoting, Hope-Lai, and Peir - based on their reputation for creditworthiness, but when the unfortunate incident occurred, each of these insurance companies refused to fulfill its obligation to compensate for the loss based on a biased opinion. They do not care about the affected business owner, and they undermine the credibility of the insurance business. In addition to the damage Bao Feng Ginseng Shop suffered being witnessed by countless people at the time, several businesses, such as Tong Yu, Zhen Yuan, and Bao Da, were willing to testify to the facts of the incident out of a sense of injustice. These letters of testimony, which had already been submitted to San Yi Public Notary Office to forward to the insurance companies, clearly show the truth. Bao Feng Ginseng Shop, whose capital and reputation are at stake, should report the facts and request your inspection and proper referral to the Chamber of Commerce for negotiation in order to maintain its losses. After investigation, it was found that the member has been operating on Lizhi Xianhua Street for more than ten years, with a good reputation. After further investigation of the true situation at the time, it was confirmed that it suffered a large loss. The insurance companies should be liable for compensating the insured amount without any doubt. As for the San Wan Public Notary Office, which said that there was less water on the third floor and more water on the second floor, it disregarded the facts and adhered to its own bias, which was inappropriate. One must know that at that time, the fire was raging, and firefighters had to use water pressure to aim upwards from below, which is an inevitable principle. Moreover, the nature of water is to flow downwards. How could it not seek the lowest point and flow downwards? This is enough to show that the notary office adhered to its own view and did not care about the pain of the victim. If this case is resolved without any reason, the credibility of foreign insurance businesses will suffer a great blow. Therefore, we have sent this letter based on the foregoing, requesting your examination and immediate notification to the Shanghai Foreign Merchants Insurance Association, and sending separate letters to Gong Yu, Sun, North Manchu, Anglo-American, Paoting, Hope-Lai, and Peir insurance companies, requesting them to compensate immediately in order to maintain their credibility. We also request that you send another letter to San Yi Public Notary Office, requesting it to adhere to the facts, recognize its notary position, and speak fairly.

Based on this, after checking the situation, it was found that Bao Feng Ginseng Shop was implicated by the negligence of its neighbor and suffered losses when the fire department's water poured down on the storage room on the second floor, which is an undeniable fact. Fair assessment and compensation should be provided. Accordingly, this letter is sent based on the situation, hoping that your company will investigate and immediately provide an assessment and compensation in order to maintain its credibility. We are deeply grateful. In addition to sending separate letters, we hereby send this to Gong Yu, Sun, Paoting, North American, Hope-Lai, Anglo-American, Peir Insurance Company, and San Yi Public Notary Office.

City Federation Appeals to the Public Works Department on Behalf of Distressed Shantytown Residents; Requests Permission for Rebuilding Pending Construction of Public Housing to Uphold Humanitarian Principles

The shantytown residents in the Linqing Road area of Shanghai's Pudong district suffered a devastating fire a few days ago. The number of victims reached over four hundred, leaving them homeless and in a dire situation. They have been appealing to all parties for days, requesting permission to rebuild their shelters for accommodation. The First Special District Citizen's Federation yesterday sent a letter to the Public Works Department stating that it had recently received a joint report from Wang Naide and others, representatives of the shantytown residents who lost their homes on Linqing Road, Pudong District. The report stated that the most painful experience for humans is to be without food, clothing, and shelter. Now, being able to temporarily erect a thatched hut to provide minimal protection from the elements is already a great stroke of luck amidst misfortune. However, good fortune never comes in pairs, and bad luck always comes in droves. At 3:30 PM on October 25th, the thatched shacks in which we resided were struck by the disaster of fire and completely destroyed. Initially, it was just a small spark, and if the fire trucks had been allowed to extinguish it, there would have been no risk of it spreading. However, the Western constables of the police station prevented the extinguishing of the fire, causing the wind to fan the flames, which quickly spread throughout the area. All forty-eight households in the district were completely burned down, and the number of victims reached over four hundred and thirty. People of all ages cried out in despair. Fortunately, the Chinese Life Saving Society provided assistance to each household, which was enough to relieve their hunger. However, after this disaster, what could be done to recover? Not only did they have no home to return to, but they also lacked the means to cook. Now, they were all sleeping amidst the ashes and were being harassed by detectives, making the oppression of the disaster unbearable. Therefore, they specifically requested the Public Works Department to speak out for them, negotiate with the Public Works Department to punish the Western constables who prevented the extinguishing of the fire, and allow them to rebuild their shelters so that the victims would not be forced to roam the streets and disrupt public order. Humans have compassion, and there is a virtue of cherishing life. They humbly requested approval, etc. The report was submitted to the Federation. The Federation previously suggested to the Public Works Department to construct public housing in stages to accommodate the shantytown residents and gradually phase out shantytowns. Before this policy is implemented, the Public Works Department should grant permission for the burned shantytown residents to rebuild their shelters to uphold humanitarian principles and avoid triggering incidents. This is our sincere hope.

Cai Yuanpei Aesthetic Education Research Institute Approved by the Central Government for Record

The purpose of establishing the Cai Yuanpei Aesthetic Education Research Institute is to promote the theories of Mr. Cai Yuanpei, establish national culture, and popularize art education, as a permanent memorial to Mr. Cai Yuanpei's academic achievements. Its preliminary work program includes:

(Academic Research) (1) The Institute may establish an art research institute to study various disciplines related to art. (2) For young people who have graduated from domestic and foreign art colleges with excellent results or who have genius and are determined to pursue further studies, the Institute will provide subsidies after passing the Institute's review. (Art Exhibition) (1) Hold exchange exhibitions with European countries. (2) Hold a national art exhibition every year. (3) Hold various temporary art exhibitions. (Academic Awards) Establish the Cai Yuanpei Scholarship to reward artistic creations and valuable writings in art. (Academic Lectures) Establish regular academic lectures, inviting domestic and foreign experts to give systematic lectures. (Book Publication) Translate famous works on aesthetics, art history, art theory, and art education from various countries around the world, and edit books on aesthetic education and periodicals. The above-mentioned tasks may be handled by a special department or committee. (Establish Art Museum and Picture Gallery) Collect famous art works and books from ancient and modern China and foreign countries for systematic display and storage. The above-mentioned tasks will be promoted in order to become China's leading art research institution. An application was previously submitted to the Central Government for record. The Central Executive Committee sent personnel to investigate and found that the progress was excellent. On that day, the reply was approved for record with No. 4850. Currently, fundraising is underway, and all parties are paying close attention. Gifts and donations are being made enthusiastically. It is reported that the provincial and municipal donations have been entrusted to the directors of the provincial and municipal education departments to be responsible for promotion.

Biscuits and Bread Prices Increase

The Shanghai Biscuit, Candy, Canned Food, and Bread Industry Association issued an urgent notice: This year, our industry has been affected by the economic downturn, and the price of biscuits has had to be reduced with great pain to facilitate sales. However, in recent years, raw materials have been rising sharply, and costs have become more burdensome. In the current situation, it will not be enough to maintain business without an appropriate increase in price. The maximum time limit for outer ports is two months, and the maximum time limit for this port is one month. Damaged and overdue goods will not be returned or exchanged. Wooden boxes (except for canned food) and tin boxes must be valued. Violators will be punished. The above-mentioned resolutions are related to the vital interests of the industry. All members of our industry, whether members or non-members, should abide by them and must not violate them. If anyone violates the regulations intentionally, they will be reported to the court for punishment in accordance with the Executive Yuan's notice and administrative regulations in order to eliminate stubbornness and maintain compliance with the law. This is hereby announced for your information.

The Beijing-Shanghai Express Train May Start Running Next Month: Two Round Trips Daily, No Special Cars Attached, Ticket Prices Remain the Same, Seats Assigned by Ticket Number

The Beijing-Shanghai-Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Bureau, to improve railway transportation between Beijing and Shanghai, is planning to launch express trains. After multiple test runs and increasing the speed to 80 kilometers per hour, the entire journey can be completed in the shortest time of four hours and twenty minutes. Based on the results of the test runs, a request will be submitted to the Ministry of Railways for approval. The internal regulations are as follows: 1. Only stops at six stations along the line: Shangbei, Suzhou, Wuxi, Changzhou, Zhenjiang, and Nanjing. 2. One round trip daily. The outbound train departs from Shanghai at 8 a.m., arriving in Beijing around 1 p.m. The inbound train departs from Beijing at 4 p.m., arriving in Shanghai around 9 p.m. The entire journey takes four hours and forty to fifty minutes. 3. Each train is limited to six carriages, including first, second, and third-class cars. Approved by the Ministry of Railways, no special cars will be attached. 4. Ticket prices remain the same. 5. Seats in all classes are assigned by ticket number. Telephone reservations will be held until one quarter of an hour before departure. Currently, the bureau has inspected the necessary locomotives and passenger cars. It is expected that the service can start running next month. It is also heard that the bureau has ordered streamlined new locomotives and passenger car chassis from abroad to be transported to Shanghai for body installation. In the future, the speed can be further increased.

Wang Yaotang, a lawyer from the police station, filed a lawsuit against her under Article 286, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Code. After being questioned by Judge Chuan Lin, she was reprimanded for using excessively cruel methods. He said, "You must have seen the play 'San Niang Teaches Her Son'. As a mother, when teaching your children, you should emulate San Niang in the play. If a child makes a mistake and needs to be beaten, you should only lightly slap the palm of their hand a couple of times. You must know that when you hit your child, your heart aches. Moreover, your child is your own flesh and blood, so you cannot bear to abuse them. Looking at this child, he has a large face and ears, and his appearance is not hateful. If you burn his face and disfigure him, it will inevitably have various effects on his future. Moreover, all capable people are mostly naughty when they are young. As long as parents teach them properly and guide them onto the right path, they will not go astray." The judge's reprimand was both solemn and humorous, and even the ignorant and foolish woman was moved. She lowered her head and admitted her guilt. Judge Chuan then sentenced her to 20 days of detention for abusing her underage biological son, with a two-year suspended sentence. During the probation period, she must bring Jinli to the police station in her jurisdiction every month for inspection so that the police station can protect and supervise the child.

Sun Yannian, an office worker from Anhui, and Sun Yonghua, a clerk, complained that the water for washing their faces in the morning was not hot enough, and ordered Zhang to pour new water a bit later, leading to a conflict. The Sun brothers then beat Zhang with fists and feet, injuring vital parts, and he died instantly. Yannian, realizing he had committed murder, fled in fear of punishment. The bureau detained Yonghua and handed him over to the Public Security Bureau, and also reported to the local court, which sent someone to examine the body for injuries and sent the body to the Zhenru forensic examination institute for an autopsy. Now, the deceased's mother, Zhang Wangshi, and the deceased's brother, Zhang Afu, have received the news and rushed here. After the Public Security Bureau questioned Sun Yonghua, who was in custody, the day before yesterday, the police sent the defendant to the local court for trial. The deceased's mother and others came to Shanghai on a long-distance bus that day, and Sun Yannian, who was on the run, was also on the same bus, planning to go to the court to inquire about his brother's situation. Unexpectedly, he was spotted by the deceased's brother, Zhang Afu (Afu had also worked at the bureau, so he recognized him). When the bus arrived at Tushanwan, Sun tried to get off the bus to escape, but was grabbed by Zhang. When the bus arrived at the Guohuo Road terminal, the police were notified and he was taken to the Ximen Public Security Bureau and then transferred to the local court. Yesterday, the prosecutor opened a preliminary investigation, ordering Sun Yannian and Sun Yonghua to be brought in, and summoning the deceased's mother, Zhang Wangshi, the deceased's brother, Zhang Afu, and witness Sun, and the police officer Ren Wansheng for a long interrogation. The two defendants were ordered to be detained pending the autopsy report and further investigation.

Ni Jintang Dies from Circumcision, Xuan Xishou Rashly Performs the Surgery and Kills Him with Anesthesia

Ni Jintang, a 25-year-old from Shaoxing, was an employee at the Tianhe Dye House at No. 38 North Zhejiang Road. Recently, Ni believed that his foreskin was too long, so he sought advice from his friend Ri Qihong, who worked as a male nurse at the Baolong. Ri then introduced Ni to Xuan Xishou, who had also worked as a nurse at Baolong Hospital and is now an accountant at the Caihua Laundry and Dyeing Shop at No. 533 Baike Road. After Ni explained his intentions, Xuan readily agreed and performed the surgery in the shop at around 8:00 PM the day before yesterday, also injecting an analgesic. Unexpectedly, Xuan rashly performed the surgery and used a strong anesthetic. By the time the surgery was completed, it was already 10:00 PM, and Ni Jintang had already died. Xuan Xishou was panicked and immediately called Baolong Hospital, falsely claiming that someone had taken poison and was in critical condition, requesting them to send a car to pick them up quickly. The hospital received the news and, without suspecting anything, immediately went to pick them up. When they attempted to save him, they discovered that the person had already died. However, after carefully examining the deceased's condition, it did not appear to be poisoning. They then examined the body and discovered the cause of death. They immediately reported it to the police station, which sent detectives to investigate. They then inquired at the Caihua Laundry and Dyeing Shop and learned the truth. They immediately arrested Tian Qihong and others and will submit them to the court for interrogation this morning. At the same time, they reported to the court, requesting an examination of the body.

Accountant Li Hongshou's Lecture: Income Tax and Accounting Improvement

Accountant Li Hongshou of the Lixin Accounting Firm gave a lecture on the implementation of income tax and its relationship to accounting improvement. The following is a record of the lecture:

Today's business operators all know that strategies of competition, monopoly, and mergers and acquisitions can only generate profits temporarily and are not long-term solutions. Therefore, they feel that the only effective long-term solution is to analyze and compare past figures from accounting to serve as a reference for the future. Therefore, accounting has become a business compass. The development of accounting can be divided into three stages. First, to ensure the completeness of bookkeeping records and to save time. Although this goal has been achieved, whether the items on the resulting balance sheet are accurate is still a question. Therefore, the second is to ensure the accuracy of valuation. However, even if the valuation is accurate and the figures on the balance sheet are indeed accurate, they cannot be clearly displayed without comparison and analysis. The state of assets and liabilities and the business situation cannot be known, nor can it be known whether the situation is improving or deteriorating compared to previous years, in order to make improvements. Therefore, the third is the comparison and analysis of the balance sheet. Advanced accounting countries have already done this. As for the history of accounting in our country, it is still in its infancy. For the first step, we have not yet been able to achieve perfection. Although most accounting scholars have vigorously promoted it, compiled series of books, and established schools, its impact is still small. Except for a small number of enterprises that have paid attention to the issue of valuation, most economic enterprises still use the amount of profit as the standard for asset valuation. In our country's industrial and commercial organizations, there is no fixed standard for the valuation of assets. When closing accounts at the end of the year, the asset and liability accounts are first roughly estimated to obtain an approximate amount of profit and loss, which is compared with the required or desired amount of profit and loss, and then the valuation standard is determined. If there is a year with generous profits, the inventory will be undervalued, more depreciation and bad debt reserves will be provided. Conversely, the inventory will be overvalued, less depreciation and bad debt reserves will be provided, or even nothing will be provided, to reduce losses or increase profits. The results of the second step are like this, and the third step can be imagined. Recently, the government promulgated the Provisional Regulations on Income Tax, stipulating that the first category is income from profit-making enterprises, and taxes are levied according to the amount of income. If the accounting is not accurate, the amount of income will also be inaccurate. If it is too high, more taxes will be paid, resulting in unexpected losses. If it is too low, less taxes will be paid, creating the suspicion of tax evasion. In the future, business operators will not be able to simply make up enough profit and be done with it. The implementation of this income tax has a tendency to promote accurate accounting, because with accurate accounting, there will be fair taxation. Therefore, I cannot help but celebrate the development of accounting in our country's future, and I especially hope that leaders in the industrial and commercial sectors will consider this early and make improvements in advance to avoid the suspicion of overpaying or evading taxes on the taxes that should be paid. However, each of the above accounting issues has its own valuation method and its own reasons, which are problems that have not been resolved by Chinese and foreign accounting scholars. Moreover, national legislation has the principle of legislation, so there must be detailed regulations in the implementation rules. If it is ambiguous, and merchants choose a method that can pay less tax, what can the government say to question it? In Article 49 of the Implementation Rules of the Provisional Regulations on Income Tax, only Article 15 stipulates that "When calculating the first category of income, the actual expenses, bad debts, depreciation, inventory consumption, public levies, and public reserve funds stipulated by laws and regulations shall be deducted from the total income, and the remaining balance shall be the net profit, which shall be taxed according to the tax rate stipulated in Article 3 of the Provisional Regulations." There are no detailed regulations for the above items. If this is the case, I am afraid that there will be many disputes between business operators and tax collection agencies in the future. I believe that there is a need to amend and supplement the articles. Please state the reasons:

1. Inventory Valuation: There are three methods for inventory valuation: original cost, current market price, and the lower of original cost and current market price. Each of these three methods has its advantages and disadvantages. Therefore, the implementation rules should either specify which method should be adopted, or not specify it, but stipulate that those who used method A last year must still use method A this year and cannot change it. If there is a change, it must be approved in advance. It must also be stipulated that the inventory should have detailed records. If there are no records, an actual inventory must be taken to serve as a basis. When filing the return, the quantity, unit price, amount, valuation standard, and inventory situation of the inventory should also be filled in in detail. Also, the quantity, unit price, and amount of the opening inventory of the current period should be the same as the closing inventory of the previous period. If this is the case, although the valuation for this year is low and less tax can be paid, when it is sold next year and the profit is high, it will still need to be supplemented.

2. Regulations on Depreciation Rate: The depreciation rate of fixed assets depends on the nature of the assets and the length of the usage period. Therefore, there are various depreciation rates, and there are many calculation methods. If there are no regulations, what should be followed? If detailed regulations are made, it would be difficult. If there is a depreciation rate that has been set in the commercial sector, it would be more convenient. The United States has established depreciation rates, which occupy more than 50 pages in the accounting compendium. At a minimum, it should be stipulated that when filing the return, the type, quality, purchase date, original cost, usable period, used period, accumulated depreciation reserves, and depreciation rate for the current period of the asset should be filled in in detail. The depreciation rate for each year should also be the same. If there is a change, it must be approved in advance.

3. Amortization of Bad Debt Reserves: From the perspective of accounting principles, there are various methods for amortizing bad debt reserves. Although it is inconvenient to specify which method should be adopted in the implementation rules of the Provisional Regulations on Income Tax, it can be stipulated that when filing the return, the sales amount, the balance of accounts receivable, the balance of accounts written off this year, the amount not recovered, and the names and amounts of each difficult-to-recover account should be filled in in detail. It must also be stipulated that the amortization method for each year should be the same. If there is a change, it must be approved in advance.

In addition to this, the division of capital expenditures and revenue expenditures should also be specified. For example, in the case of start-up expenses, should it be an asset or an expense? Article 88 of the implementation rules of the income tax in the United States stipulates that expenses at the time of the company's establishment, such as registration fees, lawyer fees, accountant fees, and all other start-up expenses, are capital expenditures and cannot be deducted from the total income of the current year. In short, the above points should be specified in detail in the implementation rules of the Provisional Regulations on Income Tax, so as to avoid disputes between merchants and the government, and to ensure that taxation is fair. At the beginning of legislation, the government naturally cannot take care of everything in detail. Furthermore, when the people are not yet accustomed to this new tax, if the regulations are too dense, it may cause a backlash. This is also the difficulty of the legislators. However, in order to avoid disputes between the government and merchants in the future and to ensure fair taxation, it will be necessary to amend it. It is best to supplement the implementation rules with the above points, because the regulations are still provisional regulations and can be amended at any time. According to the Japanese Income Tax Law, from the Meiji 20th year to the present, about 50 years, there have been two major revisions, and there have been more than 20 minor revisions. In the 17 years from 1918 to 1935 in the United States, it was also amended eight times. I also hope that the government's legislative officials will take this as a reference.

Economic Journal

One Year of the Legal Tender

— Feng Liutang

It has been one year since the implementation of the legal tender. Over this year, the effectiveness, although currency system reforms cannot be measured for their value in the short term, the visible facts are sufficient to glean some understanding. I will now discuss the achievements of the legal tender over the past year from various perspectives.

(1) Trade Has Indeed Seen Improvement

The original purpose of promoting the legal tender was to unify the issuance of banknotes, centralize bank reserves, preserve silver and prevent its outflow, stabilize foreign exchange rates and prevent fluctuations, increase the flow of domestic capital, and adjust international trade. Since the implementation of the legal tender on November 4th last year, although there have been some minor fluctuations in exchange rates with the British pound and the US dollar, their impact on trade has been minimal. Here is a table showing the trade situation for the past year. (The "past year" referred to in this article runs from October 24 to September 25 because most of the figures for October of this year have not yet been fully settled by early November. The comparison with the same period last year also refers to October 23 to September 24. Figures are in units of 1,000 legal tender dollars.)

Comparing the current year with the same period last year, imports accounted for approximately 92.5% of the same period last year, a decrease of 7.5%. Exports accounted for approximately 129% of the same period last year, an increase of 29%. The trade deficit accounted for approximately 46.5% of the same period last year, a decrease of 53.5%. In December of last year and January of this year, there was a turnaround to a trade surplus. Although this was due to the European and American situation, currency reform also had an impact. If we compare the import and export values from January to September of this year with the same period last year, the import value accounted for approximately 95.8% of the same period last year, a decrease of 4.2%. The export value accounted for approximately 128% of the same period last year, an increase of 28%. The trade deficit accounted for approximately 54.6% of last year, a decrease of approximately 45.4%. However, there is a slight difference when converted into customs gold units. (Unit: 1,000 Customs Gold Units)

Imports decreased by 102,755 thousand Customs Gold Units compared to the same period last year, exports increased by 3,089 thousand Customs Gold Units, and the trade deficit decreased by 105,844 thousand Customs Gold Units.

As for the reasons for the increase or decrease in value, among the imports, colored cotton fabrics, other than unbleached fabrics, decreased significantly. As a result, local dyeing and weaving factories in the city that had white greige fabrics available for dyeing have seen reduced imports, rising fabric prices, and hopeful profits. The large decrease in imports of rayon, sugar, and waxes is likely due to the impact of smuggling in the Eastern Hebei region. However, the increase in imports of chemical products, dyes, books, and paper, if all used in industrial and cultural undertakings, is a good sign. As for exports, the export of leather expanded greatly this year, increasing by two-thirds compared to the same period last year. As a result, the price of fur has become very expensive, with retail prices rising by nearly one time. In addition, the export of soybeans and grains was also greater than in previous years. (Grain imports were valued at 129,248,946 yuan in the same period last year, but only 45,626,294 yuan in the nine months of this year.) Cotton increased from 51,918,000 yuan in the same period last year to 69,848,000 yuan in the same period this year. Exports of tung oil and other products increased by more than 33 million yuan, totaling more than 74 million yuan. Mineral exports also increased by more than 7 million yuan, totaling 27.1777 million yuan. In addition to these, all export products, except for animals and their products, have seen considerable increases. However, although smuggling has been prevented, it has been too widespread and has lasted too long. The lower value of imported goods this year compared to last year is also a major reason, which in turn affects customs revenue.

(2) Estimation of Gold and Silver Imports and Exports and Speculation on Overseas Gold Reserves

The activity of gold and silver imports and exports during this year was greater than in the same period last year. However, last year both government and private businesses could transport gold and silver (gold was also not prohibited), while this year only the government can handle it. The situation of gold and silver imports and exports during this year is as follows (unit: 1,000 legal tender dollars):

A Gold

B Silver

It is found that the gold exports this year mostly went to the United Kingdom, while almost all silver went to the United States, and most of the silver imports came from Hong Kong. In short, during these two years (i.e., October 23 to September 25), the net value of gold exports was 34,111,100 yuan, and the net value of silver exports was 352,501,100 yuan, which is a considerable amount. Here are the silver reserves in Shanghai after the implementation of the legal tender last year for comparison. (Units: liang/yuan are in thousands, silver bars are in bars)

According to customs records, the amount of banknote movement this year was 8,456,950 Chinese silver dollars for imported banknotes and 4,585,400 yuan for exported banknotes, which are not included in the above import and export figures. Here is the total amount of silver reserves in Shanghai during this year:

According to the Shanghai Daily News of this port on October 7th of this year, Shanghai's silver reserves at the end of August were 140 million yuan. It was also said that since September to the beginning of October, silver worth 52.9 million yuan was shipped to New York and 95.06 million yuan to Hong Kong. The total is 147.96 million yuan. At the same time, 150,000 yuan from Xiamen, 1 million yuan from Jiujiang, 5.2 million yuan from Luoyang, and 70,000 yuan from Wenzhou, totaling 6.62 million yuan, were transported to Shanghai from various places. It was also said that except for the 9 million yuan held by the Japanese Bank, only 2.2 million yuan remained. In fact, the current silver reserve only needs to be 25%, that is, only 250 million yuan is needed in the 610 million yuan of cash reserves, and it should be calculated from a national perspective, so the increase or decrease in silver reserves in Shanghai is not considered important.

Regarding the import and export situation of gold and silver in China in the past, the reporter once compiled the import and export figures of gold and silver for 46 years in mid-April last year and wrote an article entitled "How Much Gold and Silver Does China Still Have?", which was published in the 130th issue of this journal. The following tables are reprinted from it, which will make the quantity of gold and silver in and out of China clearer.

Table 1: Net Amount of Gold and Silver Imports and Exports from the 15th Year of Guangxu (Silver from the 16th Year) to the 17th Year of the Republic of China (Unit: Customs Taels)

Gold Surplus 200,761,920 Silver Surplus 194,931,612

Gold Deficit 104,001,703 Silver Deficit 813,109,039

Net Surplus 96,760,127 Net Deficit 618,177,427

If 1.5 is equivalent to silver coins, then the net gold surplus is worth 145,140,325 yuan, and the net silver deficit is 930,766,140 yuan, with a remaining net deficit of 85,625,815 yuan.

Surplus 26,216,543 Surplus 228,774,141

As for how much gold our country has overseas, it is not something we can know. However, since the banknote silver reserve has been reduced to 25%, and the remaining 35% can be filled with gold, silver, and foreign exchange, all 356 million yuan of the 610 million yuan can be transferred to overseas gold reserves. According to a Reuters New York dispatch on October 20th of this year, "The US Federal Reserve Bank has allocated gold worth 1,975,000 US dollars to foreign accounts, and it is believed that this must be the result of China's sale of silver," which is also evidence of overseas deposits.

(3) Silver Coin Minting Volume of 1.95 Billion Yuan

Since October 4th of last year, the use of hard currency has been stopped, and individuals holding silver coins are limited to exchanging them for legal tender for a period of three months. Subsequently, the period was extended for another three months. After the expiration, the remote provinces were still afraid of not having exchanged them completely, so the extension was appropriately extended, and it was stopped again when it was considered an appropriate time. The influx of Western Mexican silver dollars into China was around the Ming and Qing Dynasties, and it became popular during the Daoguang period. During the Guangxu period, Zhang Zhidong, in his capacity as Governor of Guangdong, first established a factory to mint dragon-patterned silver dollars, which was the beginning of China's silver dollars. Later, various provinces imitated it, and the silver dollar policy became corrupted. In the third year of the Republic of China, the minting of Yuan Shikai head silver coins gradually became unified. Until the Central Mint started minting new silver coins in the 22nd year of the Republic of China, and minted both A and B type factory bars, after that only B type factory bars were minted, each bar was worth 1,000 silver dollars. It was completely abolished on November 4th last year, but the factory bars are still being minted. In mid-May of this year, the Sino-American silver agreement was established. In the declaration of maintaining the legal tender issued by the Minister of Finance, there was a statement about minting 50-cent and one-yuan silver coins, but it has not yet started to be minted.

How much has China minted since the dragon-patterned silver dollars? This is also what everyone wants to know. According to official records and statistics, the number is approximately as follows:

According to the above table, the total amount of silver dollars and silver bars (each bar is worth 1,000 yuan) is 1,993,586,737 yuan. This can be regarded as the total amount of silver coins since China has minted its own silver dollars.

(4) Banknote Issuance Before and After the Implementation of Legal Tender

Since the Ministry of Finance announced on November 4th of last year that "the banknotes issued by the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications are designated as legal tender, and their issuance is centralized. Banknotes issued by other banks are still allowed to circulate, but should be gradually withdrawn and replaced with Central Bank banknotes. Hereafter, each bank shall not continue to issue new banknotes, and all printed but unissued banknotes shall be deposited with the Central Bank." As a result, the issuance of banknotes by various banks in China began to be centralized. Before the implementation of legal tender, in Shanghai alone, in addition to the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications, there were seven other banks, such as the Zhejiang Industrial Bank, that issued banknotes. The situation of banknote issuance by various banks before the implementation of legal tender is listed in the table on the left (unit: 1,000 yuan):

The total number of banknotes issued by all banks was 419.58 million yuan, and all of them were taken over by the Issuance Reserve Management Committee. However, the Farmers Bank of China was specially authorized by the Central Government to issue another 100 million yuan. The issuance amount of banknotes by various banks after the implementation of legal tender is listed below: (Unit: 1,000 yuan)

The total amount of legal tender issued by the three banks in October of this year was 961,528,000 yuan. If the banknote issuance amount of the three banks in the same period last year is used as 100%, then the ratio obtained in October of this year should be 229.5%, which is an increase of one time and 29.5%. If the banknote issuance amount of the three banks in November last year is compared with the issuance amount in October this year, the results are as follows: (%)

Central 202.6 China 165.4 Communications 170.5

The increase in Central Bank banknotes is the most, with more than one time, and the rate of increase of China and Communications is similar. If the Farmers Bank of China compares its banknote issuance amount in September of this year with that of October last year, it has increased by 362.9%. It is said that the amount exceeding the limit is said to be that the issuance amount of supplementary currency coupons is not within the limit of 100 million yuan.

As for the issuance reserves of the three banks, as of October of this year, they all exceed the statutory reserve of more than 60%.

On May 17th of this year, Minister of Finance Kong also issued a declaration to maintain the legal tender. The measures are:

(1) In order to fully maintain the credit of the legal tender, the government's cash reserve part is still filled with gold, silver, and foreign exchange, and the minimum silver reserve should account for 25% of the total issuance amount.

(2) In order to facilitate merchants and people, the government will mint half-yuan and one-yuan silver coins to complete the types of hard currency.

(3) In order to enhance the consolidation of the legal tender's position, the government's cash reserves have already raised huge sums, and gold and foreign exchange will be fully increased.

It can be seen that the composition of the cash reserve for banknote issuance has been slightly changed to meet the actual needs.

It was difficult to unify the promotion of the legal tender at the beginning, because Guangdong and Guangxi still used hao yang (small silver coins). However, in August of this year, Guangdong succeeded in unification and also switched to using legal tender. There is a saying that Guangxi will implement it on November 1st.

(5) New Subsidiary Currency Emerges

Since the legal tender has been implemented, the subsidiary currency has also been reformed. The Ministry of Finance stipulates that 12 silver cents or 300 copper coins are legally equivalent to one legal tender yuan. Each large ocean (silver dollar) is equivalent to 300 wen. The exchange rate of large oceans on the market is that each yuan can be exchanged for 10 silver cents, 470-480 or even 360-370 wen, and each cent is exchanged for 240-250 wen. Before the new subsidiary currency was issued, one-cent and two-cent subsidiary currency coupons from the Central Bank, Bank of China, Bank of Communications, Farmers Bank, and Zhejiang local banks were still in circulation. On February 12th of this year, half-cent and one-cent copper subsidiary currency and five-cent, ten-cent, and twenty-cent nickel subsidiary currency were issued. However, because our country is vast, the demand for small-denomination subsidiary currency is very large. Taking the Central Bank as an example, subsidiary currency coupons accounted for 35.75 million yuan of the 305.83 million yuan issued in October of this year. Other banks such as the China, Communications, Farmers, and Zhejiang banks have not yet been included. However, provincial governments often use the excuse of maintaining domestic prices to request the issuance of subsidiary currency coupons, ranging from 2 to 3 million yuan. Recently, it has been heard that the Ministry of Finance intends to uniformly handle the printing procedures of coupons by the central government to prevent counterfeiting and to facilitate investigation. Since the new subsidiary currency was issued in February of this year, the number of coins minted by the Central Mint as of September is shown in the following table (unit: 10,000 coins):
