However, it is still not enough to distribute, so the Ministry of Finance has proposed to restore the three mints in Wuchang, Xi'an, and Anqing to mint subsidiary currency. In Tianjin, the minting of subsidiary currency was once started but eventually stopped. The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce requested that 2.5-cent copper coins be added to facilitate small change, but it has not been approved.

The maintenance of the legal price of subsidiary currency, before the old subsidiary currency (silver cents and copper coins) is completely recovered, how to adjust it should be carefully considered. However, since the exchange price of old subsidiary currency has been stipulated, Shanghai has been able to maintain it. However, the recent black market price of silver cents is 11 cents and 7 cents (per yuan), and the black market price of copper coins is 301.5 wen (per 100 yuan), which has already deviated. Zhejiang Province is also worried about the flooding of copper coins, and there is a danger that the legal price cannot be maintained. The Provincial Federation of Commerce has telegraphed the Ministry of Finance for relief. In short, it is all because the new subsidiary currency is not enough to circulate, so the old subsidiary currency is difficult to recover, and the adjustment of various banks seems to be lacking, resulting in this phenomenon. Therefore, the three banks in various places, China, Communications, and Central, should follow the original plan of the Ministry to handle the exchange price at any time, so as to promote the actual implementation and benefit the people.

(6) Currency Price Changes and Price Increases

The visible impact of currency price changes is the rise and fall of prices. Since the implementation of legal tender, prices have risen. Here are the wholesale prices in Shanghai, the prices of imports and exports, and the wholesale price indices in North China and Guangzhou to get a glimpse.

The above indices all take the 15th year of the Republic of China as 100%. From the price indices of the three parts of the country, North, South, and Central, it can be seen that after the implementation of the legal tender, prices have increased significantly. For example, the Shanghai wholesale price index in November 24 was 9.3 higher than in October, and both imports and exports were 9.0 higher. The Guangzhou wholesale price index was 10.37 higher, and North China was 6.68 higher. Later, it increased month by month, but the trend was still stable, which shows the stabilizing power of currency prices. As far as Shanghai is concerned, the export price, except for July, has not yet reached the average price of the 15th year of the Republic of China. Exported goods are all native goods, and the most sharply increased prices are raw materials, agricultural products, and animal products. The increase in production and consumer goods is still slight. Imported prices have risen sharply due to the impact of rising foreign exchange rates. The new exchange rate of one legal tender against the British pound is one shilling and two and a half pence, while one silver dollar of national currency weighs 26.6971 grams and has a fineness of 880, which is equivalent to 23.493448 grams of pure silver. According to the London silver price at that time (when the legal tender was implemented) of 29 pence and 4375 per ounce, it was worth 23 pence and 49375, but now one legal tender yuan is only worth 14 pence and 5, a decrease of 9 pence, a devaluation of about 65%. As a result, the import price index was affected, and it rose sharply from 123.7 in October 24 to 142.7, an increase of 19%. However, it has since fluctuated around 140, which shows the stability of the exchange rate. Therefore, the United Kingdom has recently established an export credit loan department to China to develop trade with China. We can also make some contributions and do not have to urgently transport cash. Japan has followed suit and will also set up an export credit loan to compete with British merchants, and we are a market for promoting goods. However, our construction is in full swing, and there are many places where foreign capital is needed. If the imported goods are mostly materials for our construction and used to generate profits, we will welcome them.

(7) Price Increases and Production Increases

Price increases can develop industry and commerce and promote the quantity of production. However, our country's situation is special. It is not only the tail end of foreign goods sales, but also after the Sino-Japanese Treaty of Shimonoseki, foreign merchants opened factories in treaty ports, holding their special power and position, which is more superior to Chinese merchants. For 40 years, it has become a situation of guests bullying the host. Therefore, this time, the implementation of the legal tender, our country's industry, has received a considerable stimulus, but foreign merchants' factories have received even more benefits. For example, in mid-to-late October of this year, yarn and flowers soared. A Japanese factory earned 100 yuan in profit per package of yarn and more than 40 yuan in profit per package of yarn, and the textile industry in North China was almost completely taken over by them. They still want to expand it. I am really worried about the future of my country's industry. Here is the China Production Index compiled by the Central Bank to see what benefits the industry has received.

(8) Cost of Living in Rapidly Rising

Price increases can also increase the burden on general life. This year, necessities in general life, such as tofu, soybean oil, pork, fish, and even vegetables, have all risen, and the increase is almost one time. In addition, flour, wheat, rice, fabrics, wool, shirts, socks, thread, blankets, coal balls, white coal, rubber, candy, food, and all daily necessities are all rising one after another. This is not surprising. Wholesale prices have risen, and retail prices will naturally follow. Therefore, the future livelihood problem is worthy of serious attention. Report on the Fiscal Situation for the 23rd Year of the Republic and Thereafter

Previously, at the Sixth Plenary Session of the Fourth Central Executive Committee and the Second Plenary Session of the Central Executive Committee, Xiangxi presented reports on the government's fiscal situation up to November 1, 1935, and July 10, 1936, respectively. Now, a comprehensive report is prepared on the financial situation during the 23rd fiscal year (from July 1934 to June 30, 1935) and thereafter for your public review.

The most noteworthy aspect of the fiscal situation during this period was the currency reform. Recalling that since the increase in the price of silver, silver continued to flow out. To preserve currency reserves, prevent the appreciation of exchange rates, and counter deflation, the Ministry implemented a silver export tax on October 14, 1934. Xiangxi has already described the details of this process in last year's financial report. However, while this measure could help achieve the above objectives, it was not a fundamental solution. Although the exchange rate did not increase as sharply as the price of silver, it continued to rise, and the phenomenon of domestic deflation intensified daily. The price index fell to a low of 90-92 between June and September 1935. Furthermore, because of unstable exchange rates, commerce was greatly affected. The government was thus compelled to adopt fundamental currency reform.

On November 3, 1935, the government announced the implementation of the legal tender (fapi) decree, stipulating that banknotes issued by the Central Bank of China, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications would be legal tender. Anyone holding silver was required to exchange it for fapi immediately. To stabilize the exchange rate of fapi at the prevailing level, the three banks were required to buy and sell foreign exchange without restriction. The plan also included reorganizing the Central Bank of China into the Central Reserve Bank and other banking reforms, as well as aligning national budget revenues and expenditures.

The currency reform can be said to have met expectations, and domestic and foreign public opinion has generally praised it. The Shanghai price index increased from 90.5 in July 1935 to 106.1 in June 1936, indicating that deflation had been curbed. The stability of the exchange rate was unprecedented, benefiting the national economy and general commerce significantly. Since the currency reform, the foreign exchange reserves of fapi have greatly increased due to the sale of silver to the US government. Domestically, since November 3, 1935, the reserves have been further strengthened by the Currency Reserve Committee's receipt of 225,000,000 yuan in silver. Recently, the political situation in the Southwest has improved, and currency reform should be extended to that region, further advancing financial unification.

Regarding coinage, important reforms were also adopted. The newly minted subsidiary coins, nickel coins in denominations of twenty cents, ten cents, and five cents, and copper coins in denominations of one cent and half a cent, were put into circulation in February of this year. The Central Mint has recently increased its efforts to mint the aforementioned subsidiary coins, with the aim of withdrawing the existing various subsidiary currencies, whether paper or copper, as soon as possible. In addition, it is planned to mint one-yuan and fifty-cent silver coins, which will be minted and issued as soon as preparations are complete.

The necessary next step in reforming the currency system is to establish the Central Reserve Bank. Once established, it will be the sole agency for issuing legal tender and the nation's only reserve depository, enabling it to control finance and lending, regulate the operations of banks nationwide, and stabilize the international value of the national currency.

During this period, budget revenues and expenditures continued to be insufficient. The reasons for this were nothing more than the economic panic, unstable currency, uncertain overseas situation, and sharp decline in international trade, resulting in a shortfall in customs revenue. The customs and salt taxes of the four northeastern provinces could not be used to repay foreign debts. Furthermore, smuggling and tax evasion in North China have become increasingly serious since the autumn of 1935. Although strict laws have been enforced, customs officials in the north are still unable to enforce the law against the illegal activities of foreigners enjoying consular jurisdiction, leading to even more rampant smuggling. The loss in tax revenue is as high as 2,000,000 yuan per week. Moreover, the dumping of smuggled goods has significantly harmed the national economy and the businesses of legitimate Chinese and foreign merchants.

To offset the loss of revenue, it has been necessary to improve tax administration, reorganize or merge tax collection agencies to reduce expenses and improve administration. Since implementation, this has been quite effective, and financial administration expenses have been reduced compared to the past. Compared to tax revenue, the ratio was 11% in 1931, 9.9% in 1932 and 1933, and 9.2% in 1934 and 1935.

In addition, the implementation of appropriate new taxes is also under study, which could increase national revenue and balance budget revenues and expenditures. Income tax regulations have already been drafted and will be promulgated and implemented soon. Inheritance tax is also being planned. The government's intention in implementing new taxes remains to avoid increasing the burden on the people and hindering the development of agriculture, industry, and commerce.

Expenditures were substantial during this period, primarily due to disaster relief for floods, the restoration of disaster areas, the bailout of banks and industrial and commercial enterprises, and subsidies to provincial and local governments, as well as bandit suppression. However, even during this difficult financial time, the government endeavored to increase funding for education and construction and to subsidize provincial governments in implementing rural reconstruction policies. Funding for the National Economic Council continued to be allocated for construction and for managing the nation's water conservancy. The government also made great efforts to assist provincial financial reforms, most notably in Sichuan Province. The province's financial chaos cannot be denied, but the government took the lead in reforming the currency system, reorganizing debt, abolishing various harsh taxes, and stabilizing finances. It is estimated that the revenue and expenditure amounts in its 1936-1937 budget should be offset.

Given the aforementioned circumstances, a budget deficit in 1934 was unavoidable. As of June 30, 1935, the total deficit was approximately 196,000,000 yuan. Excluding the 73,500,000 yuan subscribed for the bailout of banks, the actual shortfall was 122,500,000 yuan. According to preliminary estimates, the budget deficit for 1935 will unfortunately be even greater than in the previous year.

In January 1936, the government agreed with bondholders to reorganize domestic debt, agreeing on a plan to issue unified government bonds, divided into five types, with a total value of 146,000,000 yuan, to exchange for 33 types of previously issued government bonds. The main points of the amendment were to extend the repayment period. According to this plan, annual debt service costs can be reduced by 85,000,000 yuan. At the same time, a reconstruction bond of 34,000,000 yuan was issued to consolidate national finances and make up for budget deficits.

During this period, efforts to reorganize various accumulated debts were particularly active. In February 1936, the 1908-1910 Tianjin-Pukou Railway loan, guaranteed by railway and customs revenues, was announced for reorganization. In addition, other railway loans were also being reorganized. The government hopes to continue reorganizing other debts. Recognizing that the reorganization of state-owned railways is closely related to financial construction and the restoration of national credit, the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Railways jointly handled matters related to railway reconstruction and the reorganization of old debts. In the spring of 1935, a foreign engineer with extensive experience in railway administration was hired to come to China to study the conditions of our railways. His opinions were highly valuable and contributed greatly to the improvement of our railways.

The above is a general overview of the financial situation. Now, I will report separately on the affairs under the jurisdiction of the Ministry of Finance.

(Expenditure Section)

Customs

The revised customs import tariff began to be implemented in July 1934. This new tariff reduced taxes on plain cloth and certain other goods while increasing taxes on metals, machinery, and chemicals. Although the tax rates on the latter items were increased, the principle was that their sales markets would not be severely affected. The purpose of revising the tariff was to increase tax revenue and protect domestic production and manufacturing industries. Export tax rates were also revised once in June 1934, with most goods' tax rates being reduced. However, due to the treasury deficit and other financial difficulties, the government was ultimately unable to implement its planned reduction of export taxes and abolition of transit taxes during the period from 1935 to 1936. The previous year's report stated that since April 6, 1933, a 2.25% ad valorem tax had been levied on exports of various types of silver, but exports of silver dollars and ingots were not taxed. Since October 1934, a 7.75% export tax was also levied on silver dollars and ingots, along with a 10% tax on other exported silver, plus an export equalization tax to compensate for the difference between the London silver price and the official exchange rate. These various protective measures were to prevent the outflow of domestic silver due to high silver prices in foreign markets. Silver smuggling has now stopped, as foreign silver prices have recently fallen.

Regarding the surtax on imports and exports (with tax rates of 5% of the import and export taxes, respectively), the portion for disaster relief continued to be collected during this period, and the portion for subsidizing finances was extended for another year from July 1936. Customs anti-smuggling efforts were strengthened this year. There are seventy-five large and small anti-smuggling patrol vessels, which are sufficient to prevent common coastal and border smuggling. However, since the autumn of 1935, customs patrol vessels in eastern Hebei Province have faced armed resistance and been disarmed, suffering a major setback. Smuggled goods have converged in the north and cannot be stopped. The loss in tax revenue is approximately 2,000,000 yuan per week. Now, the only option is to set up anti-smuggling stations along the railway lines to prevent smuggled goods from entering.

When observing the above tax revenue figures, the following points must be noted:

(1) The normal customs office ceased operations in 1931.

(2) In January 1931, likin, restored import duties, and inland transit duties were abolished.

(3) In 1932, the customs offices in the three northeastern provinces and Dalian were occupied.

Import tax revenue in 1935 increased by 4,880,000 customs gold units compared to 1934. However, due to the high price of silver that year, the actual silver dollar revenue decreased by 10,050,000 yuan. Since the currency reform in November 1935, the exchange rate of customs gold units has increased, so the actual silver dollar revenue has also increased accordingly. The high customs gold unit revenue in 1935 was due to the increase in some tariff rates in the new import tariff of 1934, as imports were still 10% lower than before. On the other hand, although export tax revenue decreased due to lower tax rates, exports increased by 7.6% compared to 1934. Based on the current situation and the low exchange rate of the national currency, there seems to be even more hope for increased exports this year.

Salt Administration

During the period covered by this report, the salt administration progressed steadily, and revenue increased. The improvements were particularly important in anti-smuggling and salt field management. However, the growth of native salt production has greatly impacted official sales. A few years ago, only six counties produced native salt, but according to surveys, as many as 158 counties now produce it. If native salt sales are allowed to flourish, salt tax revenue will be greatly affected. The annual tax revenue in Hebei, Henan, and Shandong provinces is expected to decrease by millions of yuan. To enable official sales to compete with native and private sales, salt taxes have been gradually reduced, and irrigation projects have been undertaken to improve the soil, so that areas producing native salt can resume cultivation. In Hebei Province, a reorganization fee is collected specifically for this work, and in Henan Province, 30,000 yuan is allocated monthly from July 1934. At the same time, various suppression methods have been used, and approximately 300,000 native salt cooking pools have been destroyed in Hebei Province by the end of 1934. In Henan Province, more river channels have been dredged to facilitate cultivation. The opened canals have reached 344 kilometers. This work is still ongoing.

Salt field management work has also continued to develop. In addition to building salt warehouses, the salt field management system has been improved daily. Areas such as Changlu, Huaibei, and Shandong all have enclosure walls, highways, tax police stations, and telephone equipment to facilitate anti-smuggling.

The unification of salt administration has made further progress this year. The salt administration and anti-smuggling agencies in Sichuan were brought under the management of the Salt Revenue Inspection Office in April 1935. Sales of saltpeter and sulfur, which have been managed by salt administration agencies since 1933, have also been improving.

The foreign debt quotas, excluding the three northeastern provinces, have been remitted on schedule by all salt revenue inspection offices nationwide. The salt administration agencies in Sichuan have also resumed remitting quotas since May 1935. Therefore, the principal and interest of loans guaranteed by salt tax have been paid on schedule, and credit has become increasingly stable. The arrears of the 1908 Anglo-French loan were paid off in October 1934. The repayment of a portion of the principal arrears of the 1912 Crisp Loan has also begun.

Regarding salt tax revenue, although silver was extremely tight and various regions experienced floods in the past year, the revenue in 1935 actually increased by 8,259,000 yuan compared to 1934. The annual revenue of the General Salt Revenue Inspection Office from the second year of the Republic to 1935 is listed below:

Tax Affairs

The items subject to consolidated tax collection currently include nine types: cigarettes, cotton yarn, wheat flour, matches, cement, cured tobacco, beer, minerals, and spirits. Spirits were previously taxed under ordinary alcoholic beverages. Since January 1, 1936, consolidated taxes have been implemented, and appropriate tax rates have been established to promote the development of the spirits industry and increase tax revenue. The consolidated taxation of aerated water is also being planned. Since the implementation of consolidated taxes on cured tobacco leaves, tax revenue has increased sharply. Unfortunately, due to the lack of strict management in tobacco-producing areas, private transportation and sales are widespread, leading to the prevalence of handmade cigarettes by private individuals in these areas, which are difficult to investigate and suppress, hindering the business of legitimate merchants and significantly affecting national tax revenue. To fundamentally reorganize this situation, a method for the consolidated control of tobacco leaves has been drafted, allowing the government to control the distribution of tobacco leaves. It has been submitted to the Executive Yuan for approval and is currently being prepared for implementation. The reorganization of the existing taxes is also continuing. For example, in recent years, smuggled, counterfeit, and tax-evading imported matches made privately overseas have flooded the market. To curb smuggling, the method of affixing flower stickers to match packages will be implemented in 1936 to facilitate investigation and suppression. The mineral taxes in Sichuan and Hunan provinces have been recovered and are now directly collected by the Ministry of Finance after consultation with the provincial governments.

Furthermore, the production and sale of native wine are scattered and disorganized, and tax rates vary from province to province. Although repeated reorganizations have been carried out, a thorough reform has not been achieved. It is now planned to first abolish the current complex tax rates on Jiangsu shaojiu, Zhejiang shaojiu, and Shanxi fenjiu, which are produced and sold in large quantities, and implement a single tax collection method to achieve unification. At the same time, efforts will be redoubled on other plans that have already been initiated to gradually advance them to achieve perfection.

Tax administration has traditionally established separate agencies to manage various tax revenues, making it difficult to achieve thorough reorganization. From 1936 onward, it has been decided to reorganize and merge the various consolidated tax, mineral tax, and tobacco and alcohol tax agencies within the same region. The provinces and cities nationwide will be divided into several districts, each with a district tax bureau as the supervisory agency. Underneath it will be tax management offices and tax branch offices responsible for investigation and collection. However, for gradual implementation, a trial will be conducted first in the five provinces of Henan, Jiangxi, Hunan, Hubei, and Sichuan from October 1, 1936. The provinces that have not yet been reorganized will continue to be reorganized by the Taxation Administration, and supervisors and inspectors will be dispatched to improve the situation as needed and promote unification.

Local Finances

Recalling that the Second National Financial Conference was convened in May 1934, and a plan for reorganizing local finances was resolved. The abolition of harsh taxes and miscellaneous levies, the reduction of surcharges on land taxes, the holding of land registration, and the determination of local budgets have all gradually achieved results over the past two years, which is quite gratifying. This is not only due to the efforts of the Ministry of Finance in urging and supervising, but also to the sincere cooperation of the provincial and municipal authorities.

Recently, the financial situation in the provinces has improved significantly, especially in Jiangsu, Anhui, Hunan, Hubei, Jiangxi, Henan, Shandong, Shaanxi, and Sichuan. The central government, to the best of its ability, has been assisting the provinces in reorganizing their finances and balancing their budgets. At the same time, it has provided as much assistance as possible to rural construction in the provinces. The most effective province in reorganizing its finances is Sichuan. When the central government advanced to suppress the communist bandits, the financial situation in Sichuan was extremely chaotic. Afterwards, as the political situation gradually stabilized, financial reform followed. The Ministry of Finance made every effort to unify the currency system and reorganize the old debts in the province. Consequently, three thousand yuan of Sichuan Financial Reorganization Treasury Bonds and seventy million yuan of Post-Disaster Rehabilitation Bonds were issued one after another. The 1936 Sichuan budget has been approved by the central government and can be balanced.

Seventeen provinces and four cities (Note 1) have submitted their 1935 preliminary budgets to the Ministry of Finance. Nine provinces and one city (Note 2) have submitted their 1936 preliminary budgets to the Ministry of Finance. No less than one thousand and fifty-nine counties (Note 3) have submitted their 1935 preliminary budgets to the Ministry of Finance.

As of the date of this report, the total amount of harsh taxes and miscellaneous levies abolished and surcharges on land taxes reduced by the provinces and cities has reached 51,000,000 yuan. As for the reorganization of land tax districts, land registration has been conducted in many areas, and further progress is expected.

(Note 1) Anhui, Chahar, Zhejiang, Qinghai, Fujian, Henan, Hebei, Hunan, Hubei, Gansu, Jiangxi, Jiangsu, Guizhou, Shandong, Shaanxi, Nanjing, Beiping, Qingdao, Ningxia, Weihaiwei, and Suiyuan.

(Note 2) Anhui, Chahar, Fujian, Henan, Hunan, Hubei, Gansu, Jiangsu, Ningxia, and Weihaiwei.

(Note 3) Anhui 61, Chahar 15, Zhejiang 75, Fujian 62, Henan 111, Hunan 57, Hubei 70, Gansu 67, Jiangxi 83, Jiangsu 60, Guangxi 84, Guizhou 54, Ningxia 10, Shandong 108, Shaanxi 92, Yunnan 50.

Debt

Since July 1, 1934, in addition to the Unified Bonds and Reconstruction Bonds issued in early 1936, the following types of public bonds were issued by the Ministry of Finance:

Date of Issue　Name　Amount

April 1, 1935　Financial Bonds　100,000,000 yuan

June 30, 1935　Customs Bonds　100,000,000 yuan

July 1, 1935　Sichuan Rehabilitation Bonds　70,000,000 yuan

August 1, 1935　Consolidation of Sichuan Financial Treasury Notes　30,000,000 yuan

November 1, 1935　Flood Relief and Work Relief Bonds　20,000,000 yuan

April 1, 1936　Sichuan Rehabilitation Bonds　15,000,000 yuan

Total 335,000,000

In addition, there were Railway Construction Bonds of 120,000,000 yuan, jointly issued by the Ministry of Railways and the Ministry of Finance, used to construct railways connecting Hunan, Guizhou, Sichuan, and Guangxi provinces, and to extend the Ping-Sui and Zheng-Tai Railways. One-third of the total amount of the bond was issued in May of this year. The principal and interest fund will be allocated from the income of the newly built and extended railways, and the surplus funds from other state-owned railways used to repay existing debts, with additional subsidies from the Ministry of Finance.

During this period, the most significant reform regarding public bonds was the unification of domestic debt. The method was agreed upon by both the government and bondholders and implemented on February 1st of this year. This method not only changed the organization of public bonds but also simplified their types. The method used five types of Unified Bonds, with a total value of 1,460,000,000 yuan, to redeem the 33 types of public bonds previously issued. Although the interest rate remained at 6%, the repayment period was extended from 12 to 24 years. The repayment periods for various public bonds previously issued were mostly shorter, with approximately 70% due within six years. Therefore, the unified method could reduce annual debt expenses by approximately 85,000,000 yuan compared to the previous regulations, greatly benefiting the balancing of the budget.

The unification method included all previously issued domestic public bonds, treasury notes, and various certificates issued by the National Government, with the following exceptions:

(1) Short-term Rehabilitation Bonds. These bonds matured in March 1936. (2) 1928 Financial Long-Term Bonds. These bonds had an annual interest rate of 2.5% and matured in 1953. (3) Haihe Bonds. (4) 1935 Sichuan Rehabilitation Bonds. Although the third and fourth types of public bonds were issued by the central government, their funds were secured by local revenue and were considered local loans. The amount of the above four types of public bonds accounted for only 8% of the total unified debt.

The old public bonds were divided into five categories based on their repayment periods to facilitate the exchange of various unified public bonds. The procedures for exchanging bonds were completed on June 30th of this year.

The issuance of 6% Reconstruction Bonds of 340,000,000 yuan was also part of the unification method. This was intended to strengthen the financial position, meet the needs of construction, and cover budget deficits. These bonds were planned to be issued gradually over one or two years.

Postponement of Repayment of Commodity Loans from 1931 and 1933. On May 28th of this year, the government, with the agreement of the US authorities, signed a contract to combine the 1931 Flood Relief Loan and the 1933 Cotton and Wheat Loan into one loan, totaling US$16,608,329.99, and extended its repayment period. The Flood Relief Loan, consisting of 450,000 tons of American wheat and flour, was originally valued at US$9,212,826.56, for the relief of the 1931 Yangtze River flood and reconstruction in the disaster areas. Two-thirds, or US$6,141,884.36, had already been repaid. The remaining US$3,070,942.20 was due on December 31st of this year. The Cotton and Wheat Loan totaled US$17,086,282.48, of which US$3,548,894.69 had been repaid before May 28th of this year. The entire loan was used for construction, reconstruction, and other purposes. The loan was originally scheduled to be repaid within three years, but when the contract was signed in 1933, both parties suggested a two-year extension. According to the original contract, the principal repayment for the above two loans was to be US$8,630,000 in 1936 and US$8,421,000 in 1937. The government, due to the ongoing currency reform, hoped to temporarily reduce the burden of foreign debt, and therefore requested an extension of the repayment period, which was fortunately supported by the US authorities. The revised repayment schedule is as follows:

According to the contract signed on May 28th of this year, the government was able to reduce the amount of principal repayment in recent years, which greatly benefited public finances.

Settlement of Old Debts The long-standing issue of old debts from the Jinpu Railway loan signed between 1908 and 1910 was resolved on February 25th of this year after lengthy negotiations. Although the loan contract designated Jinpu Railway revenue as the primary guarantee, it also stipulated that customs revenue could be used as collateral. Therefore, the government also used customs revenue as a guarantee for the interest on the loan during this settlement to maintain its reputation.

At the same time, a considerable number of old railway loans were also settled. The most notable examples include loans for the Pinghan Railway, the Nanxun Railway, and the Henan Railway.

The government continues to pay attention to this complex issue of old debts, and deeply hopes to settle all other old debts in the shortest possible time.

Recently, the prices of the government's major foreign debts have been rising in overseas markets, reflecting the government's policy of consolidating national debt credit, which has achieved tangible results and is gratifying.

Central Bank

During this period, the development of the Central Bank has been rapidly changing. This can be seen from the table below.

During this period, in addition to continuing to provide the government with various domestic and foreign conveniences, the Central Bank was able to actively perform the duties of a central bank. When financial turmoil occurred frequently and the social economy was unstable, the bank, in close cooperation with the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications, advocated emergency measures to provide strong assistance to commercial banks. Since the implementation of restrictions on the export of silver in October 1934, the bank has consistently worked hard to stabilize foreign exchange rates, with significant results.

Since the implementation of the legal tender policy on November 3, 1935, the government has been urged to control the total amount of legal tender in circulation nationwide and the lending activities of domestic banks in order to stabilize the new monetary system. During the silver standard era, the export or import of silver always had the effect of regulating the market, balancing China's internal and external economic conditions. However, now that circumstances have changed, achieving proper financial regulation requires the authorities responsible for implementing monetary policy to pay close attention and plan carefully at all times.

The original text of the new monetary policy announced on November 3, 1935, stated: "The Central Bank, currently state-owned, should be reorganized into a Central Reserve Bank in the future. Its main capital should be provided by various banks and the public, so that it becomes a detached institution capable of maintaining the stability of the national currency with all its might. The Central Reserve Bank should keep the reserve funds of various banks, manage the national treasury, and store all public funds, and provide rediscounting facilities to various banks. The Central Reserve Bank does not engage in ordinary commercial banking business, but will enjoy the exclusive right of issuance after two years."

In February of this year, Xiang Xi suggested to the Executive Yuan that 60% of the Central Bank's government shares be transferred to commercial shares to meet social needs and demonstrate joint ownership with the people. At the same time, a special committee was organized to plan the reorganization of the bank into a Central Reserve Bank. The committee has conducted thorough research and submitted a report, which is currently being carefully considered by the government authorities. Xiang Xi sincerely hopes to see the early realization of the new bank.

Central Bank

Currency

Weighing the needs of modern countries and adapting to China's unique economic situation, the government's monetary policy aims to achieve a unified and sound currency system. The establishment of the Central Bank in 1928, the opening of the Central Mint in 1929, the abolition of the tael and the introduction of the yuan in 1933, the preparations for currency reform, and the implementation of the new currency system on November 2, 1935, are all steps to complete the monetary policy.

The implementation of the silver export tax in October 1934, to control the outflow of silver and prevent foreign exchange from fluctuating with foreign silver prices, was described in detail in the previous report. Without such measures, the silver reserves used to maintain the currency system would have been exhausted long ago. The catastrophic fall in prices would have been unimaginable. Considering Hong Kong, where there were no restrictions on the export of silver, the wholesale price index fell to 69.4 in August 1935, while the Shanghai wholesale price index only fell to 93.2 in the same month (both using the 1922 average as 100). This further illustrates the importance of collecting silver export tax. However, although this measure can be effective for a time, it is not a fundamental solution for stabilizing finance. Since its implementation, the smuggling of silver has not stopped, foreign exchange has continued to rise, currency has become tighter, and domestic silver prices are still affected by fluctuations in foreign silver markets. If we compare the monthly average exchange rates of British and US dollars with the parity calculated based on London silver prices in the past three years, and calculate the difference between the market price and the parity, we have the following table:

(Note 1) The figures before November 3, 1935, are based on forward prices, and the figures after are based on recent prices.

After the promulgation of the silver export tax, the exchange rate decreased slightly, but soon returned to its rise. By the spring of 1935, it continued to rise to US$0.42 or GB£0.205 per yuan. The highest prices in the first half of October 1934 were US$0.38 and GB£0.185. There are several reasons why the exchange rate continued to rise. China's foreign exchange has long been affected by fluctuations in foreign silver prices, and it is impossible to break this connection in a short period of time. Silver is still silver, and foreign silver prices will inevitably rise along with it, which cannot be suppressed by banning exports. Currency continued to tighten, and the Shanghai wholesale price index was 99.9 in February 1935, but fell to 90.5 in July of the same year. Moreover, foreign silver prices were 15% to 65% higher than domestic silver prices, and the profit from smuggling was very high. Given the vastness of China's borders, coupled with the obstacles of extraterritoriality and concessions, prevention was very difficult. The sign of silver outflow was extreme financial tightness. The impact was enough to raise foreign exchange and lower prices. Although silver interest rates fell slightly after the Lunar New Year settlement in February 1935, this was not evidence of ample funds, but rather due to the exhaustion of funds in the market at that time. The delay in construction and the obstruction of government financial arrangements were profound and significant.

At that time, the signs of economic crisis in China became increasingly evident. Bond prices plummeted, real estate prices fell, and the weaker Chinese and foreign firms went bankrupt one after another. Those who勉强勉强maintained were also greatly weakened, leading to an increasing and spreading of bankruptcies and unemployment. This situation was most severe in the spring and autumn of 1935. During this period, the government, with the cooperation of the Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications, raised relief measures and allocated 25,000,000 yuan in treasury notes to lend to various industries to solve the urgent need, and the danger of national economic bankruptcy was fortunately avoided.

The most important measure taken by the government was to reorganize the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications, increase government capital, and enable them to cooperate with the Central Bank in providing relief to industry and commerce and reforming the currency system, thereby achieving twice the result with half the effort. After the government shares in the Bank of China were increased to 15,000,000 yuan, the total capital was 40,000,000 yuan, 50% of which was government shares. After the government shares in the Bank of Communications were increased by 10,000,000 yuan, the total capital was 20,000,000 yuan, 60% of which was government shares.

In early 1935, the government was well aware that thorough currency reform was the only way to stabilize finance. To prevent currency tightening and save China from the whirlpool of economic panic, this was the only option. Therefore, the reform plan was approved. By October, the situation had become even more dangerous, so on November 3, the government resolutely implemented the new currency system policy and promulgated the legal tender measures, stipulating: (1) Stabilizing foreign exchange, approximately based on the foreign exchange market price at that time; (2) The banknotes issued by the Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications are designated as legal tender and issued centrally; (3) Silver is nationalized; (4) The Central Bank is reorganized into a Central Reserve Bank to become a detached institution; (5) Improve the commercial banking system and find ways to increase its activity; (6) Consolidate public finances so that the national budget can balance revenue and expenditure again after eighteen months. (The declaration and notice of the implementation of the new currency policy are appended below.)

The day after the new currency system bill was announced, the British Ambassador issued an order requiring all British merchants and residents in China to comply and prohibiting the use of silver to pay debts, with violators being considered criminals.

The government also found that China's old subsidiary coins were extremely complex, so it promulgated the subsidiary coin regulations and ordered the Central Mint to mint subsidiary coins of 20 fen, 10 fen, 5 fen, 1 fen, and 1/2 fen, which were issued on February 10th of this year. In order to facilitate merchants and residents, silver coins of 1/2 yuan and 1 yuan will be minted to complete the types of coins. The number of subsidiary coins minted by the Central Mint in the first half of this year is listed below:

Type Number Face Value

20 Fen Nickel Coins 11,618,544 2,323,708.80 yuan

10 Fen Nickel Coins 18,183,668 1,818,366.80 yuan

5 Fen Nickel Coins 50,737,202 2,536,860.10 yuan

1 Fen Copper Coins 119,980,000 1,199,800.00 yuan (Note)

1/2 Fen Copper Coins 41,160,000 205,800.00 yuan

Total 241,679,411 8,084,535.70 yuan

(Note) Includes 3,100,000 pieces (worth 31,000 yuan) minted in December 1935.

However, various currencies are circulating in China, and they must be gradually withdrawn. The number of new subsidiary coins required will naturally be very large. It may take several years to completely replace the old ones.

The government's measures to reform finance have achieved good results and are now being vigorously promoted to achieve complete success. Since the announcement of the legal tender bill, the Ministry of Finance has established a Legal Tender Issuance Reserve Management Committee in Shanghai, and approved the establishment of branches in Tianjin, Hankou, Guangzhou, Xi'an, Jinan, Changsha, Qingdao, and other places, responsible for the custody of the legal tender issuance reserve fund, and at the same time responsible for the issuance and exchange of legal tender. Regarding the exchange of legal tender, the Ministry of Finance has formulated measures for the exchange of legal tender and regulations for the management of silver used in silver products, which are progressing smoothly. In order to prevent improper speculation and excessive price increases, price stabilization committees have been established in various places to crack down on them.

The implementation of the new currency system has been initially successful. The Shanghai wholesale price index was 90.5 in July 1935, 94.1 in October, 103.3 in October, and 106.1 in June 1936. The Lunar New Year customs closure was passed safely, and there was no disturbance in the market. Export trade in the first half of this year increased by a quarter compared with the same period last year. Customs revenue initially showed an increase, but began to decrease slightly due to the impact of rampant smuggling in North China.

Since the implementation of the new currency system, national capital has become more concentrated. Foreign exchange is extremely stable. As of the end of June of this year, the Issuance Reserve Management Committee has collected 225,000,000 yuan of silver, in addition to the original silver held by the Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications. In November 1935, the Chinese government signed a contract with the US government to sell 50,000,000 ounces of silver at a price of US$0.65 per ounce, which was shipped to the US in December of last year. In May of this year, a second batch of silver was sold to the United States. This measure was taken to regulate foreign exchange and stabilize exchange rates, in order to strengthen people's faith in the new currency system. The United States' support for China's new currency system not only benefits the Chinese people, but also greatly benefits foreigners who trade with us.

In May of this year, in order to increase the security of legal tender, the Ministry of Finance stipulated that the cash reserve for legal tender should still consist of gold, silver, and foreign exchange, with the minimum amount of silver reserve accounting for 25% of the total issuance. At the same time, the Ministry of Finance announced the abolition of restrictions on the use of silver in silver products. (The declaration and ministerial order are appended below.) Since the implementation of the new currency system, the total issuance of the Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications has increased from 427,000,000 yuan to 856,000,000 yuan (calculated on June 27th of this year), an increase of 429,000,000 yuan. Of this amount, 139,000,000 yuan was used to redeem banknotes issued by other banks in the past, and the remaining 290,000,000 yuan was prepared with 172,000,000 yuan of redeemed silver, gold and foreign exchange, and bonds recovered from the market. The total issuance in China as of the end of June of this year is listed below:

Total issuance of the Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications 856,000,000 yuan

Other banks 165,000,000 yuan

(Farmers Bank 71,912,000 yuan)

(Previous banks that have not been redeemed 93,000,000 yuan)

Total 1,021,000,000 yuan

The central government has spared no effort to consolidate the currency policy of various provinces. For example, after the reorganization of the various currencies originally circulating in Sichuan Province, they were all redeemed with banknotes from the Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications. The Southwest is also planning to change to the silver dollar system, unifying the national currency system.

Overall, China has made significant progress in stabilizing finance in the past year. With a solid foundation, if there is no obstruction from changes in the international situation, the national economy can be expected to prosper day by day.

Budget

The year 1935 has just ended, and the final accounts will take some time. Here, we will briefly list the general situation of revenue and expenditure for the five years since 1930, based on the report of the Accounting Department of the Ministry of Finance, for comparison (Note 1):

The annual repayment of the Boxer Indemnity, except for the expenses of secured debts, is generally not included in the above table. Most of the government's borrowing over the years has been used to repay old debts. However, the new bonds issued were issued at a discount, resulting in extremely high interest rates in practice, and the national tax revenues designated as security for the new debts have also been increasing day by day.

The fiscal deficit in 1935 was much larger than in the previous year. There are several reasons for the increase: (1) The large-scale smuggling in North China in the past year, the frequent international disputes, and the weakening of people's purchasing power have all reduced the amount of imports, resulting in a sharp decline in customs revenue; (2) Severe floods in rivers, serious disasters, repair dams and relief, and increased expenditures; (3) The economic downturn is becoming more and more profound, and the cost of rescuing the silver industry and the industrial and commercial sectors is also huge; (4) The cost of subsidizing various provinces and local governments is still huge; (5) The suppression of communist bandits in the Northwest and Southwest cannot be delayed; National defense construction is a matter of survival and cannot but be done to the best of our ability.

Military expenditures and debt expenditures have been the main items of annual expenditures, as can be seen in the table on the left:

Education and construction expenditures Although the national treasury's financial resources have been depleted in recent years due to coping with various unexpected events and other uses, the Ministry of Finance's concern for the progress of education and construction has not diminished. The Ministry of Finance firmly believes that in order to increase tax revenue, it is necessary to first improve the people's productivity and improve their daily lives. Fortunately, through the Ministry of Finance's efforts, expenditures on education and construction in recent years, including highways, railways, water conservancy, public health, and rural relief, have increased, which is gratifying.

The figures listed in the table above include disaster relief expenses. The subsidies paid to the provinces are not included. Most of the subsidies to the provinces are used to support the development of local education, the implementation of economic construction, and the abolition of exorbitant taxes. The amount is also quite considerable, with 32,001,332.81 yuan in 1933 and 55,488,072.42 yuan in 1934, and the education and construction expenditures for these two items increased even more in 1935.

The national budget for 1936 has been promulgated. The budgeted amounts for revenue and expenditure for 1935 and 1936 are listed separately below for comparison:

In the past seven or eight years, the government has spared no effort to develop and nurture tax sources, such as the revision of customs tariffs, the consolidation and improvement of salt administration, and the creation of a unified tax system, all of which have been effective. The progress of various tax revenues can be seen in the table below:

Although a portion of the increase in tax revenue over the years is due to the gradual direct collection of national taxes in various places by the Ministry of Finance, the required collection expenses have also increased accordingly. Moreover, since 1929, internal rebellions have occurred frequently, and the communist disaster has spread, resulting in huge costs for suppression. In addition, continuous disasters and flood control and relief require money everywhere. The cost of the Yangtze River flood relief in 1931 exceeded 70,000,000 yuan, and the estimated property loss was 200,000,000 yuan, which greatly affected national tax revenue. Since the loss of the Northeast, tax revenue has been lost accordingly, resulting in the failure to allocate funds for the joint agreement for foreign debts secured by customs and salt from these four provinces. Moreover, commerce between the Northeast and the inland provinces has been relatively smooth, but it has been hindered by this, causing great damage to the government's tax revenue and industry and commerce. In the past two or three years, due to the impact of various economic downturns, not only has tax revenue failed to increase, but temporary expenditures on relief and other costs have increased sharply.

Conclusion

Since 1933, the financial hardships our country has faced are unprecedented in modern history. This is due to frequent natural disasters, rampant communist banditry, and the need for substantial funds for disaster relief and bandit suppression. Coupled with the impact of the global economic recession, our country has suffered even more. Furthermore, accumulated debts from previous years have made the financial situation even more difficult than before. However, even amidst such immense difficulties, the Ministry of Finance has still been able to allocate additional funds to promote construction, most notably in areas such as education, highways, railways, water conservancy, public health, rural relief, and other productive enterprises. In addition, efforts have been made to consolidate old debts to maintain the credibility of national bonds. Fortunately, the government adopted the most appropriate measures regarding the national financial organization, responding calmly to changes, and with the united assistance of the people, was able to avoid collapse and move towards stability. Moreover, the financial industry is now gradually showing signs of vigorous growth. Once it fully recovers, its future will be unlimited.

The government's financial reforms and economic construction have now been decisively implemented. If there are no external troubles, more significant progress can be made. Furthermore, the Southwest problem has recently been completely resolved, so there is no further issue of financial unification.

To achieve further progress, the government must base its financial policy on the following principles:

(1) All unnecessary or unproductive expenditures should be curtailed to provide funds for productive and construction purposes.

(2) Identify and train tax collection personnel to improve administrative efficiency.

(3) Consolidate existing taxes and levy sound new taxes to increase revenue without increasing the burden on the people.

(4) Reform local taxes to align them with national taxes.

(5) Improve the banking system and promote rural credit systems to facilitate the recovery of the rural economy.

(6) Complete the unification of the currency system and maintain the stability of the national currency exchange rate to stabilize the financial situation.

(7) Settle old debts to maintain the credibility of national bonds.

In recent years, the government was forced by circumstances to focus all its efforts on meeting urgent needs. However, in the future, it will shift its focus towards economic construction. To achieve this goal, a more effective budgeting system must be established to control various uses of funds. However, the government's aspiration in finance is not merely to balance revenue and expenditure, but also to make finance healthier day by day, leaving surplus resources to develop domestic economic resources and improve people's lives.

The financial situation for the fiscal year of 1934 and thereafter is presented as follows. Respectfully submitted to:

The Central Political Committee and the public. Kong Xiangxi, Minister of Finance. August 1, 1936.

The Eight-Character Bridge in Zhabei

— Rong Yu

Before the January 28th Incident, the Eight-Character Bridge in Zhabei, apart from the residents living nearby, probably even rickshaw pullers familiar with the routes couldn't find it. It was truly remote and desolate here, with no bustling shops, no well-to-do residents. Who would pay attention to it? When the January 28th war broke out, the 19th Route Army deployed along the west of the bridge, and the Japanese army attacked from the east of the bridge. The intensity of the fighting was no less than in Jiangwan and the railway station, with repeated losses and gains. For this small piece of land, countless lives were sacrificed. Therefore, the three words "Eight-Character Bridge" were widely reported in newspapers and circulated among the public. So, it is true to say, "The name of the Eight-Character Bridge was bought with fresh, red blood."

Why did the two armies fight so desperately for this small Eight-Character Bridge? Because in terms of terrain, it was indeed the throat of Zhabei along the east. Because there is a very long Sha Jing Port in Zhabei, starting from Jiangwan in the north and ending at the Huangpu River in the east. Within the Zhabei area, the two armies faced each other across this river. The southern end of the Eight-Character Bridge is Yokohama Road, and the Japanese army's attack began along this road. If this bridge were crossed, then the communication line between the North Railway Station and Jiangwan would be cut off immediately, and the bustling area of Zhabei would immediately be liable to be occupied. Therefore, the attacking side paid attention to this, and the defending side did not dare to slacken, thus creating repeated fierce and terrifying offensive and defensive battles.

However, if you look at the end of this bridge daily, you would hardly believe that war had happened near this bridge, and that it was so fierce. The bridge surface, about ten feet wide and twenty feet long, lies flatly on the dirty Sha Jing Port. The river water is as black as ink; in the middle, there is an awful stench; sometimes a few awning boats are parked in the river. At the east end of the bridge is Shuidaidian Road, and at the intersection stands a hundred-year-old ginkgo tree, showing its majestic angularity. At the west end, there are a few small houses, opening a few small shops, that end leads directly to Liuying Road. The north and south are Yokohama Road, which is also unusually deserted. Most of the tall Western-style houses were destroyed by artillery fire and have not been restored; private villas and gardens are also desolate and dilapidated. In this point, it can be proved that the name of the Eight-Character Bridge is truly not accidental.

Miss Killer

— Zhu Ying

Miss Killer, the one mentioned here is not Miss Tao, who is still in Hangzhou prison, but another lady who kills without using weapons.

The Miss Killer mentioned in this article is a relative by marriage. She was betrothed in childhood, and when she was eight years old, her parents died, so she lived in her fiancé's family. Childhood sweethearts, innocent and carefree, her feelings with her fiancé were better than brother and sister. Later, her fiancé's family sent her to school, from elementary school to middle school, and she actually became a high-achieving student in a certain middle school. Her fiancé fully intended to marry her after she graduated from middle school, but one month before her graduation ceremony, she suddenly hired a lawyer and asked her fiancé to cancel the marriage contract that her parents had arranged for her when she was a minor. Her fiancé was suffering from some minor illnesses at the time. After receiving this blow, his illness worsened, and he died before the lawsuit was over.

After her fiancé's death, her termination of the marriage contract was easily resolved. Then she formally married her lover. Her husband was already married, but for her sake, he forced his legal wife to divorce. His legal wife was a woman who couldn't think things through. After the divorce, the more she thought about it, the narrower her perspective became, so she secretly swallowed raw opium and committed suicide. But she and her husband lived happily together for only a year, and she discovered many shortcomings in her husband. The most unbearable thing for her was his fondness for prostitution, so she resolutely demanded a divorce. After more than three months of litigation, the divorce was successful, but her husband received this stimulus too deeply. He felt too sorry for his ex-wife, and his mind became perverted from thinking about it day and night. Finally, one night, he jumped down from the roof of a five-story building and ended his life.

It was on the very night that her ex-husband committed suicide that she was holding a wedding with a banker in a large hotel. This banker, who had married such a beautiful socialite, was overjoyed. In terms of money, not only was every request granted, but sometimes, even without a request, he would find ways to provide for her. After entering the social scene, she had never met such a straightforward man, so she was extremely fortunate to have married such a good husband. However, her good husband was originally strong on the outside but weak on the inside. After living together for a year, he had already accumulated a lot of deficits. In order to make up for them, he secretly embezzled public funds to engage in speculative transactions. Unexpectedly, every battle was lost, and the deficits could not be made up, so he hardened his heart and committed suicide in a hotel.

In the hands of this Miss Killer, four people have been killed in just three years. Currently, she is looking for her next partner. But I don't know, in this world, which unfortunate person will become her fifth victim? I am sweating for her future husband.

My Mother's Death

— Yi Mei

A mother's love is great, it is unconditional, not built on material things, but unlucky me, suddenly lost this love recently, what a painful thing that is!

My mother gave birth to my two brothers. My father passed away when I was only four years old, and my younger brother was only two years old. Our family was poor, without any savings. My mother worked hard with her own hands, enduring hardship to raise us. Later, I went to live with my maternal grandparents, and my mother also came to depend on them. Since the death of my maternal grandparents, my mother lived separately with my younger brother, but still came to visit and care for us from time to time. For twenty or thirty years, she has been like this. My mother's kindness is so great, it is truly limitless.

In recent years, my brother and I lived in Ximen, and I rented a house in Dananmen, not far away. Every few days, I would definitely go to visit her. Although I am at the age of ambition, my mother still sees me as a child. When she sees me arrive, she always takes out candy and pastries from the jar to treat me. When the weather is cold and snowy, seeing me wearing a Western suit, she always says it is so thin, isn't it too cold? It's better to wear a camel hair robe, it's warmer. Although I am working during the day, my salary is not high, so I have to bury myself under the lamp at night, writing articles to earn money, to supplement my income. When my mother found out, she often advised me: "Don't use your brain power too much, rest earlier at night, exhaustion can cause illness, you must pay attention!" My situation is frustrating, and I often have negative thoughts. My mother used gentle persuasion to ease my worries. If my thoughts did not change, my mother was so anxious that she cried and said: "My son, please don't be like this, later when mother is old, I still need to rely on you to live. "At this time, tears involuntarily flowed from my eyes. My mother also shed tears in return. This scene is still vivid in my memory, but from now on, no one will care for me, no one will be considerate of me. Because this mother who cared for me and was considerate of me has left me and passed away.

My mother was usually very healthy. She got up early to help my brother's wife and the servants with housework, never shying away from fatigue. But since last year, she suddenly suffered from stomach trouble, sometimes it would get better, sometimes it would get worse, her body suffered greatly. In addition, last winter, my nephew Jia Rong, out of patriotism, committed suicide in anger. Jia Rong was my mother's most beloved eldest grandson, and my mother felt extremely sorry. From then on, she was depressed, until this autumn when she suffered from dysentery and also suffered from external symptoms. She repeatedly sought treatment from famous Chinese and Western doctors, who all said that dysentery was still treatable, but this external symptom called "cancer" was very tricky. But later the wound gradually became smaller, and we were all overjoyed, thinking that my mother had escaped death and there was hope for recovery. We were just preparing to wait for my mother's body to recover, and have a good family celebration, but who knew that this family celebration became a dream, that death god stretched out his giant spirit hand and grabbed my mother away!

After my mother got sick, every time the setting sun was dim, I would return from Gordon Road School, and I would first go to Songxue Street in Ximen to comfort her in front of her bed, or hold my mother's hand to see if she had a fever or chills. But I always believed that medicine was omnipotent, especially the technology of Western medicine, who knew that medicine in the current era is still pitifully young. I am pained by my mother's death, and can't help but curse those so-called famous doctors.

That day, I was late because of something at school, it was already after six o'clock in the evening. Unexpectedly, as soon as I stepped into the door, my mother was already dying. As soon as my mother saw me arrive, she immediately waved her hand and passed away. It turned out that around four o'clock, my mother had been moaning and nearly dying. But in a hurry, the family couldn't find my telephone number, so they had to say to my mother: "Don't go! Ji Yun hasn't returned yet. "Ji Yun is my alias, my mother often called me Ji Yun. After being mentioned this, my mother seemed to have taken a stimulant, opened her eyes wide, and looked out the door, looking straight until I stepped into the room, made this last farewell, and then closed her eyes and passed away. This tragic impression is truly deeply imprinted in my mind, and will not be diminished in this life. From now on, no matter in any time of fragrant flowers and singing birds, any scenic area, any scene of bright lights and fine wine, any moment of joy, as long as I suddenly think of this tragic impression, I will suddenly be stunned and teary. Gui Zhenchuan's biography of his deceased mother said: "There are people who have no every year, Heaven, how painful!" I truly embrace the same feeling.

The Gold and Silver Cave of Guangxi

— Chen Tianci

Anyone who has been to Guangxi must admire the Gold and Silver Cave.

The Gold and Silver Cave is located south of the city of Si'en Prefecture. There, two peaks stand facing each other, with a high cliff. On the cliff are inscribed the eleven large characters: "Gold seven li, silver seven li, only in seventy-seven li." The characters are written with extraordinary strength, and it is unknown when they were carved. Below the cliff is a land temple, built by the local people. There was a geomancer who said that there was gold and silver energy in the land, so the local people searched in many ways, but the result was still nothing. Later, it was known that there was another cave on the side peak, in which the accumulated silver was seen. So the local people built wooden frames to climb up, went inside to pick it up, but could not carry it out, or picked it up and threw it out, and it disappeared as soon as it hit the ground. Someone once led a dog in, wanting to tie the silver to the dog's body and lead it out, but when leading it, the dog had to bark, and when it came out, the silver on the dog's body was also gone, so the local people all said that there was a spirit in the cave, and later they all warned each other not to enter. It is said that it is still like this today.
