Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talk

Arson

— Jianping

The Shanghai Bund has nine schools of thought and three classes of people, with all kinds of news happening that is beyond the ordinary. Making a living by arson is just one of many.

Logically speaking, people are "compassionate" and "merciful" animals. They think about everything in a good way, and there is no reason to cut off their own chances of survival. The so-called "life after death" is nothing more than the meaning of "burning the boat," and it is definitely not destroying yourself first and then talking. However, this is just a dead principle, and people as smart as humans will "live" and use it. We know that the origin of the insurance business is because people want safety. Fire insurance is to prevent fires, hoping to pay a small amount of insurance premiums; you can save yourself from constantly worrying and holding the mentality that if it burns, you have insurance, so you are willing to eat a little immediate loss. Originally, this is a shortcoming of people, but the fire insurance business survives on this shortcoming. However, "there is always someone better," although the fire insurance business uses the psychological shortcoming of human complacency, some people instead use the shortcoming of this shortcoming to give it a hard time. Therefore, from this point of view, making a living by arson is nothing strange.

The local news in this city recently reported: Cracking down on the arson machine. It roughly said: A Russian in Shanghai secretly manufactured arson machines specifically to set fires for others, seeking compensation from insurance companies. It has recently been cracked, and one person was arrested with the case, followed by three more people. The evening newspaper continued to report that, according to the confession of the seven arrested criminals, one person first entrusted the auction house with the auction of fur and other items, deliberately raising the price, and a partner bid for 6,000 yuan. He then used this voucher to purchase 6,000 yuan of fire insurance, mixed it into the warehouse, and then tried to set a fire to seek compensation. From this, we can know that the organization of this "arson business" is not as simple as we thought. It is not only organized, but also planned. At the same time, what we should not ignore is that they even spare no effort to manufacture arson machines to carry out this conspiracy. It can be seen that this matter is not unusual.

Now that it has been cracked, the excitement-loving Shanghai people have of course gained a new perspective. The results of the crime and the sentencing are not within the scope of this topic, and we will not care about it. Here, we just want to write some thoughts on the cause and effect of this crime.

Crime has become organized, which is the result of modern civilization and so-called scientific management. At the same time, turning it around, if we only passively prevent it beforehand, or severely punish it afterwards; that will not reduce the number of criminal cases. On the contrary, it will only make criminals more and more careful and alarming day by day. This is because the question of whether this problem is solved by sentencing is raised. For example, arson, although it occasionally happened in the past, was nothing more than the evolution of "when poor, one seeks change, and when change, one achieves success." It will not be as organized and methodical as this case is now. It is conceivable how serious it is to manufacture machines for arson. But, why do they have to "rack their brains" for a crime? Why waste such energy on planning crimes? The answer is very simple, it is nothing more than: "They want to live, they have to eat; and this society does not give them food, so they have to "take risks"." Because this "arson" can "make a living" after all, and it is still "profitable," they have to do so for life. Then, if we can understand this, there is nothing strange.

Stealing Crops Thief

— Shihua

On the dark green horizon, stars twinkled with milky white light, flying aimlessly in the sky. Behind the clouds, a light shone through, and the dark green horizon showed violet; later, it added gold and rose, and the sky became a gentle pale purple.

The moon, which was about eight or nine points round, scattered milky white light. The wild and bright river surface was strangely quiet, and the waves were extraordinarily calm. The moon was reflected on the water surface, still a round one.

"No wonder the moon is so good tonight, it turns out it's only the eighteenth." The young man, who was about fifteen or sixteen years old, was quite strong, but he was a little short. His face was round, and he smiled like a cat. His wide mouth really made people laugh.

"I can't tell you're pretending to be gentle. Go to sleep quickly, be careful someone will steal crops tonight." This one was taller, but his body was not as strong as the other one. Even if you compared their arms, the difference was far. At this time, he was lying on the mat, with half of his body covered with broken cotton, and he was pulling the sitting companion next to him with all his strength, meaning for him to lie down.

"Don't worry, with such a good moon tonight, are you still afraid that those "petty thieves" will come to steal crops?"

"Taogen, it's not that I, Alongsheng, am getting old today. Maybe there will be a big fog tonight. If someone steals it, you'll be unlucky."

Taogen was half-believing and half-unbelieving, but he had no choice but to lie down.

The night was already very light. In the wilderness, it was quiet, like death.

It really was foggy! The moon seemed to be covered with a thick veil, and the light faded as a result. The ground also seemed to be covered with a layer of black yarn. The river surface was filled with thick moisture. The few trees along the river, as if they had climbed onto a thick spider web, were heavy, and the wind could not penetrate.

The fog was really deep, and the earth was so dark that it could not be darker. It was pitch black, and even the dogs were afraid to bark. The wind was blowing in the west rice field, and you could only hear the whistling sound, but you could not see the shaking thing. If someone was on the road at this time, they would definitely step into the river.

"Listen, there's someone." The sound was so small that it was almost inaudible.

Page 20

inaudible.

"Um—" Wiping his eyes, Taogen thought he hadn't opened them, but he didn't know it was the dimness of the fog.

"Oh!" A good beating. Taogen raised his fist in the air, but he didn't see it.

"Follow me." The two of them quietly walked on tiptoes.

Over there, there was still the "crick crick" sound of harvesting, which was strangely slow, like an unskilled novice.

The two of them quietly walked to a place not far from the harvesting sound. The crop-stealing thief didn't seem to know yet, and was still harvesting. At this time, Alongsheng shook his body, took out the small knife, and shouted "Come on," and rushed over there. Taogen also followed quickly.

The crop-stealing thief was strangely weak. Alongsheng gently grabbed him and threw him to the ground. Four fists fell on the strangely thin body, like chopping wood.

The crop-stealing thief silently let them beat him, without fighting back or begging for mercy. He was as if he was dead.

"Oh, why don't you make a sound? Alongsheng, light a fire and take a look, don't let him play dead, hum, this cunning thief." Saying that, he threw another punch.

"Ah! Sin." The remaining half of the match was thrown on the ground and extinguished. Alongsheng sat down indifferently.

"What's wrong?" Taogen thought he had been hit by a hidden weapon.

"It's your grandpa!"

"What?"

"It's your grandpa!"

"My grandpa?"

The two children helped the thief on the ground up. The old man's face was covered with mud and blood, and he was panting more fiercely than anything else. It was really Taogen's grandpa.

At this time, he seemed to feel a little more comfortable, and weakly opened his eyelids a little, and then closed them again. Only heard him saying softly.

"Tao'er, you are too loyal."

The Madman

— Yun Hai

Early morning. The sky was just beginning to turn white.

The only rooster in this waterside village, the one raised by the old rich man, was crowing loudly. Its voice was so resonant that it woke everyone from their dreams.

From the boathouses (Note), women with disheveled hair emerged, stretching and yawning, to begin their day's work. Some went to the opposite Luo Village to help out with chores, living the life of those on land; others, whose husbands had gone to sea for the fishing season, scattered in small boats to Yangjia Port to cast nets, hoping to catch some fish to sell at the Longtou market the next day for rice money. Thus, they began their busy day. Some were spreading nets, others were grabbing oars and heading to the seaside to push their boats. Everyone focused all their energy on their work, humming a few salty sea shanties to harmonize with the air.

The sun emerged from the water after taking a bath, straightening up, its eyes staring as if it barely recognized the land after a night's separation. The sunlight was not yet scorching, it was gentle and loving, caressing the reddish-brown skin of the people, as if encouraging them: Take courage! Living is about struggle!

Sister-in-law Fu and Third Aunt were teaming up for an early morning netting session. Because it was the end of autumn, the early morning tide in the first part of the month was rushing in. Catching a netful under the tide's head would yield at least twenty or thirty catties, enough to sell for a good price and eat well for a few days. Isn't that right? Everyone wants to climb higher, one day at a time, hoping for the next day to be better than the last.

"Isn't Brother Afu up yet? People get lazy when they rest. Today is a big tide, it would be better to catch more if he could come and help. My Aniu is young and not..." Third Aunt said to Sister-in-law Fu, counting the days on her fingers as if remembering something.

"Yes, I'll go and call him!" Sister-in-law Fu replied casually, but she didn't immediately go back to call her husband. She was hesitating. She knew very well what kind of temper Brother Afu, who had been unemployed for several months, had. He loved to argue and scold, and in the middle of the night, he would go to play mahjong and drink shuangzheng liquor miles away from the village. When the game broke up, he would stagger back, humming and swaying, arriving home just in time to get on everyone's nerves. Yesterday, he didn't come back until one or two in the morning, just before dawn. If she disturbed him now, wouldn't she be asking for a slap? Therefore, Sister-in-law Fu hesitated.

The headstrong Third Aunt didn't forgive her, and shouted, "Go if you're going! It'll be too late when the sun is over the hill!"

"Go! Go!... Um, Third Aunt, you know his temper hasn't been good lately. I'm afraid I won't get anything good, and might even get punched!"

"Afraid of your own husband revealing your secrets, isn't he as lazy as a snake in hibernation? And this is for everyone's meal..."

Sister-in-law Fu got angry, and without waiting for the headstrong Third Aunt to finish speaking, she hurried back to their broken boathouse.

At this moment, the whole waterside village was alive with sunlight. Although prolonged hunger plagued it, making it look like a dying yellow dog, panting and drooling, it sometimes appeared quite imposing. The row of pine trees along the river neatly guarded this famine-stricken village. At this moment, they looked even more beautiful as the wind swayed them.

Sister-in-law Fu squeezed into the broken boathouse and whispered, "Hey! Hey! Wake up! It's a big tide this morning, Third Aunt said she needs your help! Hey, hey!"

"Ugh..." He lazily turned to his side and went back to sleep.

After Sister-in-law Fu had impatiently nagged for a few moments, she finally stirred up our Brother Afu's sleepy anger. With sleepy eyes and a drowsy head, he remembered what the group had said at Dexing Restaurant last night, and suddenly jumped out of bed, lunging at the unlucky Sister-in-law Fu, shouting and yelling—

"You motherfucker, why did you wake me up? May your line die out, eighteen generations of your mother's rotten cunt, you're all a jinx, bringing bad luck into the house, damn rotten thing, I'll beat you to death, you old whore..."

Sister-in-law Fu was driven out without rhyme or reason. He followed behind like Guan Gong, dragging a broom. Even Brother Afu, known for his kindness, was beating his wife. The news spread through the village like a doomsday announcement, and those who remained came out of their boathouses to watch the show. Third Aunt, the troublemaker, stuck out her tongue and dragged her boat towards the sea. By the time Sister-in-law Fu arrived, she had already grabbed the oars and was preparing to sail to Yangjia Port.

Brother Afu's eyes bulged as he stared blankly as Sister-in-law Fu cried and shouted as the fishing boat set out. His cursing gradually subsided.

"You damn rotten cunt, raised by a whore, wanting me..."

He couldn't curse anymore. He lowered his head, as if ashamed, and walked away awkwardly with his hands clasped together. Unknowing children followed behind him, throwing small stones and cursing.

"Look, look, a turtle beating his wife!"

"Don't look at me as if I'm young, you are worse than animals when I grow up!"

He couldn't stand the rhymes the children were making up. He clenched his teeth, red veins popped up on his forehead, and he clenched his fists, wanting to beat them up for a moment of satisfaction.

Bang—a stone hit his brow, and even his heart ached faintly. So, he took a big step, his big round eyes blazing with fire, his hands outstretched like banana leaves, chasing after the mischievous kids.

The children were so frightened that they hid in their mother's arms, and the mothers closed the doors, scolding their children: "Don't play with that good-for-nothing madman."

(Note) When people who live on water come ashore, in addition to thatched huts, most move their broken boats ashore, which is called a boathouse.

Journey

— Lu Jia

A meandering line of trains cut through the July plains like a streak of ink.

The barren plains on the north bank of the Yellow River resemble the wilderness of the north, devoid of a single blade of green grass or verdant tree. Yellow earth stretches to the horizon, blending with the hazy, yellowish-sand-covered sky. The smoke from the thatched roofs rises vigorously into the evening sky, filled with sunset clouds. The colors of the twilight sky are ever-changing: streaks of orange-yellow and crimson-purple transform into flocks of sheep and camel caravans. The round, large sun sinks like a ball of fire into the long river. Travelers covered in yellow sand carry heavy luggage, trudging wearily along winding paths, as if a gust of wind could sweep them away.

The train car has an excessively high temperature and an excessive density of passengers, yet the train lacks high speed. A lone traveler, leaning against the window, gazes at the night falling over the fields, feeling a bit impatient and lonely.

The monotonous sound of the wheels accompanies the monotonous ticking of the watch on their wrist. Time passes slowly, and in the dim, weak red light, a group of vulgar faces, honest and simple faces, have two timid, tired eyes. The yawns and the coarse snores of those sleeping slumped against the backs of their seats are not a comfort but rather a repulsive sensation that makes long-distance travelers feel like vomiting. Disgusted, they avert their eyes, focusing on the quickly passing telephone poles and the simple, monotonous wilderness of the evening.

The earth revolves with the setting sun as its center and the steel rails as its circumference. The train runs along the arc of the circumference. Fan-shaped fields rotate, endlessly, seemingly never-ending. For travelers, calculating time and distance is the most foolish thing to do; the clever thing is how to pass the long hours, or how to let their destination arrive without them realizing it.

Page 21

Shanghai Postal Administration Mail Dispatch Timetable

All Shanghai branch offices can handle registered express airmail and exchange savings and other services.

Page 22

Page 23

But for a lone traveler, this is too difficult, too difficult.

A person sits in a dark corner of the train car, their chin propped on their hand, probing the width of the desolate plains with gloomy, cold, sharp eyes. The wild scenery gradually shrinks automatically, and when it shrinks until it presses against the window, the speed seems even slower. The twilight wilderness is even more monotonous, even more lonely. Besides the thick shadows and faint shadows, it is difficult to distinguish objects even if one wants to.

One can only feel the cool breeze from the fields by stretching one's head, face, and arms out the window. The thick air stagnating in the train car does not mix with the outside, mixed with the sweat and earth smells of the villagers. The clumsy bodies of the northerners cast swaying shadows on the ground, and their heavy breathing makes the air even more turbid. The lone traveler continues to stare at the thick night outside the small window, frowning, their anxious gaze piercing the night as if to tear it apart.

Passing through a wild station, flickering lights and swaying figures float on the station. The train pants as if holding its breath. Some people get off, some people get on. The lanterns outline a hazy silhouette of the wild station, and people swim in and out of the interplay of light and dark. Even though the stop is only for a minute or two, travelers feel it is a remarkably long time, and they become a little anxious.

Restlessly shifting in their seat, waiting for the train to roar, they rush headlong into the dark depths of the night. The solitary person stares with goat-like eyes, seemingly without feeling, facing the face of the night pressed against the window.

The endless journey, the endless time, is accompanied by the beating of the lone traveler's heart, the monotonous sound of the watch, and the monotonous sound of the engine.

Remnants of Sound

Ding Wane's Shanghai Opera, which is broadcast on New Sound Radio (1380) from 2:30 PM to 3:30 PM every afternoon, has recently organized a class of children's Shanghai Opera, all of whom are children over ten years old, and it is said that yesterday they had already joined the Dayunlou Singing Team, and the audience was very welcome.

After moving to McDougall Road, China Radio Station (1080) will broadcast a special program in conjunction with Lao Jiefu Silk and Satin Bureau on the tenth of this month. I think the wonderful programs held by the United Huade Pharmacy will definitely be a grand event.

The Social English in Books taught by Shanghai English School is very popular among people in the society. Therefore, in addition to teaching a class at Li Shude Hall (1940) from 5:00 PM to 5:50 PM, English experts will broadcast from 7:30 AM to 8:30 AM. Those who want to purchase the book can go directly to the school at 671 Edward Road or purchase it from the painting department of this newspaper. If there is anyone who wants to transfer it, please provide the price and machinery description. This editorial office will collect it and arrange a meeting if it is suitable.

Movies

"Guangling Tide" Interlude "Reviving the Nation"

"Guangling Tide" is a famous novel, and Yihua Company has now selected Chen Kengran to write and direct it. It has been in production for half a year and cost 80,000 yuan. The interlude in the film, "Reviving the Nation," is majestic and passionate. According to this song, it was composed by Yan Gefan and the lyrics were written by Huang Jiping.

(1) Compatriots! Compatriots! My dearest compatriots! Awaken the masses, work for the country, if you don't get up again, the country will not be protected, the enemy is encroaching step by step, who allows you to be happy and carefree, everyone work together to eliminate the enemy, saving the country is today!

(2) Liberation! Liberation! The Chinese nation wants liberation! For nearly a hundred years, national affairs have been chaotic, iron shackles and chains have been heavy and difficult to bear, imperialism is ferocious and cruel, like tigers, leopards, and wolves, everyone work together to break free from the shackles and sing hand in hand!

(3) Freedom! Freedom! Strive for national freedom! People all over the country, take neat steps, aim at the goal and share the enemy's hatred, unite the world's small nations, stand up and work hard. Everyone work together, our hot blood flows, return our freedom.

Fei Mu's New Work "Wolf Mountain Bloodshed Record" Hunter - Zhang Ji

Shanghai will screen "Circus"

Human beings are equal, there is no discrimination based on race or ethnicity. Whether red, yellow, or black, all have equal rights. This is the theme of "Circus." But such a great theme is like a flower of blood, it unfolds in a relaxed tone, and even the most prejudiced person can hardly say it has propaganda implications, which cannot but be attributed to skill. Soviet directors are now widely using "form to assist content" to supplement "content determines form." If this sentence is correct.

"Circus" tells the story of an American female artist who is ostracized by "civilized people" and deported for having a black child with a black man. She fled to the Soviet Union, and because of her superb skills, she was loved by the masses in this country of national equality. Although her leader publicly announced her "secret" (relationship with a black man), the Soviet audience instead picked up the black child and sang a lullaby.

The greatness of the musical number is due to the fact that it is state-run, and even the United States pales in comparison.

After this film passes inspection, it will be screened at the Shanghai Grand Theater.

"Drama Joint Society" Organizes Staff Entertainment Programs

The "Drama Club" has been renamed "Drama Friendship Society" by a resolution of the executive committee. The reading room will be officially opened today for public viewing. At the same time, it will organize staff entertainment programs and prepare to set up "Drama Art Teaching Classes." The first week's entertainment programs are: Monday night at 8:00 PM Ouyang Yuqian will lecture on "The Private Lives of Foreign Dramatists"; Friday night at 7:00 PM Lu will organize a world-famous music concert; Sunday night at 8:00 PM Tang Na Lan Ping will organize a chocolate tea party, welcoming staff to participate freely, but the chocolate tea party requires a fee of one dime.
